From the chapter of oaths: section of breach by swearing: If one swears 'I will not swear,' he breaches by a conditional statement (ta'liq) because the pillar exists without the addition due to its absence, except if he suspends on acts of the heart or the coming of the month for those who menstruate. His statement 'because the pillar exists' means the pillar of the oath, which is suspending the consequence upon a condition. And his statement 'without the addition' means to the time, like 'you are divorced tomorrow' – he does not breach by it because there is no pillar, so the condition of breach, which is swearing, does not exist because it is a cause in the present, so it is a delayed effective pronouncement, so it is considered like an immediate one like 'you are divorced today.' As for suspension, it is not a cause in the present, whether it is his own action or another's or the coming of time and the woman is among those who menstruate, and whether the consequence is divorce, emancipation, Hajj, or a vow, except if he suspends the consequence upon an act of the heart like 'you are divorced if you wish' or 'if you love' or 'if you are pleased,' or upon the coming of the month like 'if the beginning of the month comes' and the woman is among those who have months without menstruation, then he does not breach because the first is used for ownership not suspension, hence it is confined to the sitting, and the second is used to indicate the time of the Sunnah because it is the time of occurrence of sunni divorce in her case, so it is not purely for suspension. Therefore, he does not breach by suspending divorce upon divorce like 'you are divorced if I divorce you' due to the possibility of intending to narrate the reality of his being the owner of divorcing her, nor by 'if you pay...' because it is an interpretation of kitaba, so it is not purely for suspension, nor by 'you are divorced if you menstruate a menstruation' because it is a name for the complete one and it does not exist except with a part of purity, so it can be made an interpretation of sunni divorce, similarly twenty menstruations because what follows is a time for sunni divorce in general, for if he divorces her in a purity in which he did not have intercourse, then he returns to her and leaves her until she has twenty menstruations, then says 'you are divorced for the Sunnah' while she is menstruating, it occurs as sunni after this menstruation, so it is not purely for suspension. And he does not breach in these cases because swearing by divorce is prohibited, and interpreting the speech of a rational person in a way that removes the prohibition or reduces it is better, and here it is possible to interpret it in a way that it bears of ownership or interpretation, so it is not interpreted as swearing by divorce. And his statement 'and it is not necessary that I menstruated' means that where he breaches despite the possibility of making it an interpretation of bid'i divorce, like if he said 'you are divorced for bid'a' because it is not suitable as an interpretation due to its multiple types like occurring during menstruation or during a purity in which he had intercourse or a purity before that and the like, and it cannot be made an interpretation for all due to contradiction, nor for one due to ignorance, so specification is impossible, unlike sunni which is one type. And also it is not necessary that 'you are divorced if the sun rises' even though the meaning of the oath, which is obligation and prevention, is missing, because they are the fruit of the oath not its pillar, and the shar'i ruling in contracts is based on form not fruit, as if one swears not to sell and sells a void sale or with an option, he breaches because the pillar exists even though transfer of ownership is not established. As in Sharh al-Farisi summarized. So the exceptions from their statement 'he breaches by suspension' are six issues, let them be memorized.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on when a conditional statement (ta'liq) constitutes a breach of an oath not to take an oath. The author explains that generally, any conditional pronouncement that includes the pillar of an oath (suspending a consequence on a condition) is considered an oath and thus breaches the vow. However, there are six exceptions where the conditional statement is interpreted differently, such as when it involves acts of the heart (wish, love, pleasure) because those are used for ownership not suspension, or when it specifies a time (like 'at the beginning of the month') for a woman who menstruates because that indicates the time for sunni divorce. Other exceptions include conditional divorce upon divorce (due to possibility of narrating reality), conditional emancipation upon payment (interpretation of kitaba), conditional divorce upon menstruation (interpretation of sunni divorce), conditional divorce upon twenty menstruations (similar), and conditional divorce upon sunrise (because the fruit of the oath is missing). The Hanafi position emphasizes interpreting the speaker's words in a way that avoids or minimizes the prohibited act of swearing by divorce. The passage is from a commentary expanding on the matn.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): A conditional statement where a consequence (like divorce) is made dependent on a future event; considered the pillar of an oath.
حنث (hanth): Breach or violation of an oath; committing the thing one swore not to do.
إضافة (idafah): Addition or specification of time (like 'tomorrow') that makes the pronouncement an immediate but delayed effective pronouncement, not a suspension.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The six exceptions where ta'liq does not breach an oath are those involving acts of heart, time specification for sunni divorce, conditional upon divorce, kitaba, menstruation, and sunrise – all based on istihsan to avoid the prohibition of swearing by divorce.

Immediate vs. Suspended Divorce in Oath Scenarios
Ruling on immediate vs suspended divorce with istihsan and khul' trick

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when a man says 'you are divorced unless I divorce you, you are divorced' and distinguish between connected and separate utterances.

Core Idea
An immediate divorce cancels a suspended one if uttered together, by istihsan to fulfill the oath.

When a man swears an oath involving divorce, the wording can create both an immediate and a suspended divorce. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that, by juristic preference (istihsan), the immediate divorce takes effect and negates the suspended one. Understanding this ruling is crucial for counting divorces and avoiding unintended triple divorce, especially when a husband uses a compensation divorce (khul') to fulfill his oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband says: 'You are divorced unless I divorce you, you are divorced.' This creates both a suspended divorce (conditional on non-divorce) and an immediate divorce.
The suspended divorce is the first part; the immediate is the second part.
2
Recognize the two divorces
The suspended (mu'allaqah) is conditional; the immediate (munajjizah) is unconditional.
Hanafi terminology: munajjizah vs mu'allaqah.
3
Apply the ruling by istihsan
By istihsan, only the immediate divorce takes effect because the time of uttering it is considered part of fulfilling the oath. The suspended is canceled.
Istihsan overrides the apparent literal meaning to achieve the oath's purpose.
4
Distinguish connection vs separation
If the utterance is connected (mawsul), only immediate counts; if separate (mafsul), both count. 'Connected' means no significant pause.
This affects the total number of divorces.
5
Analyze the khul' trick dispute
In Al-Muhit, a man swears: 'If I do not divorce you today three times, you are divorced three times.' He offers a compensation divorce (khul') for a thousand dirhams, but the wife refuses. The apparent riwayah says three divorces occur; Abu Hanifa's narration says no divorce occurs (the fatwa).
The key is whether the compensation divorce counts as a valid divorce for fulfilling the oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك أنت طالق طلقت هذه الطلقة) تصريح بما فهم من قوله «وسکت» ومراده أنها تطلق المنجزة لا المعلقة استحساناً، ولا يعتبر زمان الاشتغال بالمنجزة سكوتاً لأن زمن البر مستثنى بدلالة حال الحلف لأنها إنما تنعقد للبر فهو المقصود بها ولا يمكن إلا بجعل هذا القدر مستثنى فهو نظير من حلف لا يسكن هذه الدار وهو ساكنها فاشتغل بالنقلة من ساعته بر وفائدة وقوع المنجزة دون المعلقة أن المعلق لو كان ثلاثاً وقعت واحدة بالمنجز فقط إذا كان موصولاً، فلو كان مفصولاً وقع المنجز والمعلق. وفي المحيط : لو قال لامرأته إن لم أطلقك اليوم ثلاثاً فأنت طالق ثلاثاً فحيلته أن يقول لها أنت طالق ثلاثاً على ألف درهم فلم تقبل المرأة، فإن مضى اليوم تقع الثلاث في قياس ظاهر الرواية لأنه تحقق شرط الحنث وهو عدم التطليق لأنه أتى بالتعليق والتعليق غير التطليق، وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنها لا تطلق وعليه الفتوى لأنه أتى بالتطليق لأن هذا تطليق مقيد لأنه تطليق بعوض، والمعاوضة ليست بتعليق حقيقة، والمقيد يدخل تحت المطلق فينعدم شرط الحنث ا هـ .
His statement: 'You are divorced unless I divorce you, you are divorced' – this divorce takes effect as immediate, not suspended, by istihsan. And the time occupied with the immediate is not considered silence because the time of fulfillment is excepted by the indication of the state of swearing, because oaths are only made for fulfillment, so that is their purpose, and it is not possible except by making this amount excepted. It is similar to one who swears 'I will not live in this house' while he is living in it, and he busies himself with moving out from that moment; he fulfills. And the benefit of the immediate taking effect without the suspended is that if the suspended were three, only one occurs by the immediate if it is connected; if it is separate, both the immediate and the suspended occur. And in Al-Muhit: If a man said to his wife 'If I do not divorce you today three times, you are divorced three times,' his trick is to say to her 'You are divorced three times for one thousand dirhams' and the woman does not accept. Then if the day passes, the three occur according to the apparent of the riwayah because the condition of breach is realized, which is non-divorce, because he came with suspension and suspension is not divorce. And it is related from Abu Hanifa that she is not divorced, and upon this is the fatwa, because he came with divorce, because this is a restricted divorce because it is a divorce for compensation, and exchange is not truly suspension, and the restricted is included under the absolute, so the condition of breach is nullified. End.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage discusses a scenario where a man says to his wife: 'You are divorced unless I divorce you, you are divorced.' The ruling is that the immediate divorce takes effect, not the suspended one, by istihsan (juristic preference). The reasoning is that the time taken to utter the immediate divorce is not considered silence; rather, it is included in the time of fulfillment of the oath. The benefit of this ruling is seen when counting divorces: if the suspended divorce were three, only one occurs with the immediate (if the statement is connected), but if the statement is separate (disconnected), both the immediate and suspended take effect. The passage also cites a scenario from Al-Muhit: if a man swears 'If I do not divorce you today three times, you are divorced three times,' he can trick the oath by offering a divorce for compensation (khul'), which is considered a valid divorce and thus avoids the breach. According to the apparent riwayah, the three would still occur, but a narration from Abu Hanifa says she is not divorced, and this is the fatwa, because the compensation divorce is a restricted divorce and not truly a suspension.

Key Terms
منجزة (munajjizah): Immediate or unconditional divorce, taking effect at the moment of utterance.
معلقة (mu'allaqah): Suspended divorce, conditional upon a future event.
موصول (mawsul): Connected speech where the immediate and suspended are uttered without interruption.
مفصول (mafsul): Separate speech where there is a noticeable pause or gap between utterances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only the suspended
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
By Hanafi istihsan, an immediate divorce cancels a suspended one if uttered together, fulfilling the oath and preventing unintended triple divorce.

Six Exceptions to Conditional Divorce in Hanafi Law
Listing six exceptions where conditional phrasing does not result in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five explicit exceptions (and the mentioned sixth) where a conditional phrase does not result in divorce, and explain the Hanafi reasoning for each.

Core Idea
Not all conditional phrases cause divorce—some are explanations, not suspensions.

In Hanafi law, a conditional phrase like 'if X, then you are divorced' typically triggers divorce upon X. However, the Hanafi school recognizes exceptions where such phrasing is interpreted as an explanation (tafseer) of a legal state, not a conditional suspension (ta'liq). This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists five explicit cases and mentions a sixth, all of which do not result in divorce. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly applying Hanafi law on conditional divorce.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule
Know that under Hanafi law, a conditional statement like 'if X, then you are divorced' is considered a valid ta'liq (suspension) and causes divorce when X occurs.
The general principle is that the apparent condition triggers divorce.
2
Identify the exceptions as tafseer
Recognize that the exceptions are cases where the statement is interpreted as a tafseer (explanation) of a past or present situation, not as a genuine condition. For example, explaining the terms of kitabah or the length of 'iddah.
Tafseer nullifies the suspension effect.
3
Memorize the first exception: suspending divorce on divorce
If a husband says 'if you divorce, you are divorced,' it does not cause divorce because it could be a narration of what has already occurred.
The possibility of hikaya al-waqi' (narrating reality) prevents it from being a valid ta'liq.
4
Memorize the second exception: kitabah clauses
Phrases like 'if you pay, you are free; if unable, you are a slave' are interpretations of the kitabah contract, not conditional divorce.
Kitabah is a contract of manumission, so the statement defines its terms.
5
Memorize the third and fourth exceptions: menstruation statements
Saying 'if you menstruate one or twenty times' is interpreted as explaining the 'iddah period. The phrase 'it is not incumbent if you menstruate' fails as an interpretation of bid'i divorce due to its variety, so it becomes pure suspension but still does not cause divorce.
The third is valid tafseer; the fourth is an attempted tafseer that fails but does not trigger divorce.
6
Memorize the fifth exception: impossible condition
A condition like 'if the sun rises' does not cause divorce because the condition (sunrise) is not directly related to the ability to carry or prevent—the pillar of ta'liq is incomplete.
Since the condition is irrelevant to the divorce ruling, it does not effect a valid suspension.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولهذا لم يحنث بتعليق الطلاق بالتطليق لاحتمال حكاية الواقع، ولا بإن أديت فأنت حر وإن عجزت فأنت رقيق لأنه تفسير الكتابة، ولا بإن حضت حيضة أو عشرين حيضة لاحتمال تفسير السنة، ولا يلزم إن حضت لأنه لا يصلح تفسيراً للبدعي لتنوعه وتعذر التعيين فتمحض تعليقاً، ولا إن طلعت الشمس لأن الحمل والمنع ثمرة فتم الركن دونها ا هـ . فالمستثنى من قولهم حنث بالتعليق ست مسائل فلتحفظ
And for this reason he is not considered to have divorced by suspending divorce on divorce, due to the possibility of narrating reality; nor by 'if you pay then you are free, and if you are unable then you are a slave' because it is an interpretation of kitabah; nor by 'if you menstruate one menstruation or twenty menstruations' due to the possibility of interpreting the sunnah; nor 'it is not incumbent if you menstruate' because it is not a valid interpretation of the bid'i divorce due to its variety and impossibility of specification, so it becomes pure suspension; nor 'if the sun rises' because carrying and preventing are a result, so the pillar is completed without it. So the exceptions from their statement 'he is considered divorced by suspension' are six issues, so memorize them.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage lists six exceptions where a conditional phrase does not count as a divorce (حنث). The general rule is that a conditional statement like 'if X, then you are divorced' results in divorce upon the condition. However, in these six cases, the phrase is interpreted as a mere explanation or narration, not a suspension. For example, 'if you pay, you are free' is interpreted as explaining the terms of kitabah (contract of manumission). Similarly, 'if you menstruate' could be explaining the waiting period ('iddah). The sixth exception, 'it is not incumbent if you menstruate', is not a valid interpretation because the 'bid'i' divorce has many types, so it becomes pure suspension – but it is still listed here as an exception because it does not cause a divorce? Actually, the text says 'falyahfaz' (so memorize), indicating these are cases where one is not considered divorced. The exact nature of each exception is clarified in longer commentaries.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the divorce upon a condition, such that the divorce takes effect only if the condition occurs.
تفسير (tafseer): An explanation of a legal state, not a conditional suspension; e.g., explaining kitabah or 'iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

How many exceptions to the rule that conditional phrasing results in divorce are claimed in this passage?
A) Four
B) Five
C) Six
D) Seven

Key Takeaway
Six types of statements that appear conditional are actually explanations and do not cause divorce in Hanafi law.

Immediate Divorce Despite Conditional Phrasing: The Case of 'ma lam utallik'
Explanation of immediate divorce by istihsan and hila for conditional triple divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of istihsan to interpret conditional divorce phrases as immediate, and identify the mufta bihi position in the hila case of conditional triple divorce.

Core Idea
Conditional divorce can be immediate by istihsan; a khul' offer may be a valid hila.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses two interconnected rulings. First, the husband's phrase 'You are divorced as long as I do not divorce you' followed by an immediate 'You are divorced' is treated as an immediate, not conditional, divorce by istihsan. Second, a clever legal trick (hila) to avoid a conditional triple divorce by offering a divorce for compensation is examined, with a difference between Zahir al-Riwayah and Abu Hanifa, the latter's view being the relied-upon fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic structure
Recognize that the phrase 'ma lam utallik' is a conditional clause suspending divorce on the husband's own future action.
Apparent qiyas would treat it as conditional, but istihsan overrides.
2
Apply the principle of istihsan
Understand that istihsan interprets the phrase as immediate divorce because the oath's purpose is fulfillment, and the time of the divorce utterance is excepted.
The analogy to a housing oath clarifies the exemption.
3
Analyze the hila case
Consider the scenario where a husband says 'If I do not divorce you today three times, you are divorced three times' and then offers a khul' (divorce for compensation) which the wife refuses.
The issue is whether the offer counts as a divorce for breaking the condition.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the Zahir al-Riwayah view (condition breached) with Abu Hanifa's view (condition not breached because the khul' offer is a restricted divorce).
The key is whether ta'liq is considered talaq.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text states 'wa alayhi al-fatwa' on Abu Hanifa's position that she is not divorced, which is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This shows preference for practical leniency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : أنت طالق ما لم أطلقك أنت طالق طلقت هذه الطلقة) تصريح بما فهم من قوله «وسکت» ومراده أنها تطلق المنجزة لا المعلقة استحساناً، ولا يعتبر زمان الاشتغال بالمنجزة سكوتاً لأن زمن البر مستثنى بدلالة حال الحلف لأنها إنما تنعقد للبر فهو المقصود بها ولا يمكن إلا بجعل هذا القدر مستثنى فهو نظير من حلف لا يسكن هذه الدار وهو ساكنها فاشتغل بالنقلة من ساعته بر وفائدة وقوع المنجزة دون المعلقة أن المعلق لو كان ثلاثاً وقعت واحدة بالمنجز فقط إذا كان موصولاً، فلو كان مفصولاً وقع المنجز والمعلق. وفي المحيط : لو قال لامرأته إن لم أطلقك اليوم ثلاثاً فأنت طالق ثلاثاً فحيلته أن يقول لها أنت طالق ثلاثاً على ألف درهم فلم تقبل المرأة، فإن مضى اليوم تقع الثلاث في قياس ظاهر الرواية لأنه تحقق شرط الحنث وهو عدم التطليق لأنه أتى بالتعليق والتعليق غير التطليق، وروي عن أبي حنيفة أنها لا تطلق وعليه الفتوى لأنه أتى بالتطليق لأن هذا تطليق مقيد لأنه تطليق بعوض، والمعاوضة ليست بتعليق حقيقة، والمقيد يدخل تحت المطلق فينعدم شرط الحنث ا هـ .
His saying: 'You are divorced as long as I do not divorce you – you are divorced, this divorce has occurred' is an explicit statement of what is understood from his saying 'and he was silent' – his meaning is that she is divorced immediately, not conditionally, by istihsan. And the time of occupation with the immediate divorce is not considered silence, because the time of fulfillment is excepted by the indication of the situation of the oath, because oaths are only made for fulfillment, so it is the intended purpose, and it is only possible by making this amount excepted. It is similar to one who swore not to live in this house while he was living in it, then he busied himself with moving out immediately – he is considered to have fulfilled the oath. The benefit of the immediate divorce occurring instead of the conditional one is that if the conditional divorce was three, only one occurs with the immediate one if it was connected (mawsul); if it was separated (mafsul), both the immediate and conditional occur. And in al-Muhit: If a man said to his wife, 'If I do not divorce you today three times, then you are divorced three times,' his trick (hila) is to say to her, 'You are divorced three times for one thousand dirhams,' and she does not accept. Then if the day passes, the triple divorce occurs according to the apparent ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah, because the condition of the breach (hanth) is realized – which is not divorcing – because he uttered a suspension, and suspension is not divorce. But it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that she is not divorced, and upon this is the fatwa, because he did utter a divorce – because this is a restricted divorce (talaq muqayyad) since it is a divorce for compensation, and compensation is not truly a suspension, and the restricted is included under the absolute, so the condition of breach is not realized. End quote.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage discusses two related issues. First, if a husband says 'You are divorced as long as I do not divorce you' and then immediately says 'you are divorced', the wife is divorced immediately, not conditionally, by istihsan. The time spent uttering the immediate divorce is not considered silence that violates the oath. The proof is that oaths are intended for fulfillment, so the act of fulfillment is excepted. Second, a tricky case: if a husband says 'If I do not divorce you today three times, you are divorced three times', the trick (hila) is to say 'you are divorced three times for 1000 dirhams' (a khul' offer). If she refuses, does the condition apply? According to Zahir al-Riwayah, the triple divorce takes effect because he did not actually divorce (the suspension is not a divorce). But a narration from Abu Hanifa says she is not divorced because offering a divorce for compensation is a restricted divorce, and the restriction is included under the absolute, meaning he did divorce. The fatwa is on Abu Hanifa's view.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas; here, it leads to interpreting the phrase as immediate divorce.
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending the divorce upon a condition.
حيلة (hila): Legal trick to avoid a negative consequence; here, offering divorce for compensation to break the condition.
طلاق مقيد (talaq muqayyad): A restricted divorce, such as one contingent on payment (khul').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the hila case from al-Muhit, if the wife does not accept the khul' offer, what is the mufta bihi ruling according to the passage?
A) The triple divorce occurs by the end of the day.
B) The wife is not divorced.
C) Only one divorce occurs.
D) The husband must divorce anyway.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the principle of istihsan can override apparent qiyas to favor the intention of the oath, and intra-madhhab disputes may be resolved by fatwa preference for practical ease.

Conditional Divorce Before an Event: When It Is Legally Meaningless
Analyzing the case of ajnabiyya (non-wife)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a conditional divorce with a month before an event is said to a non-wife, and explain why it is لغو (meaningless).

Core Idea
A divorce condition before a future event is invalid if the marriage does not yet exist.

The passage begins with a fundamental distinction: if a man says to a woman he has not married 'You are divorced one month before Zaid's arrival,' the statement is legally meaningless. This is because divorce requires an existing marriage; the condition presupposes a marriage that is not yet present. The author explains that whether marriage occurs before or after the month, the divorce cannot take effect. This foundational principle sets the stage for the more complex intra-Hanafi dispute when the statement is made to an actual wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and parties
The statement 'You are divorced one month before Zaid's arrival' is addressed to a non-wife. Recognize that there is no marriage at the time of utterance.
2
Understand the condition for divorce effectiveness
Divorce requires an existing valid marriage. Since the marriage is absent, the statement has no legal effect.
This ruling is unanimous among jurists.
3
Analyze possible timings of marriage
If marriage occurs before a month, the divorce would be like 'you were divorced yesterday' (invalid). If after a month, the divorce would coincide with marriage, which is impossible. Thus, the statement is inherently invalid.
The condition 'one month before' is tied to the marriage's existence.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

. كذا في العتق والإمام معهما في القدوم إذ المعرف الحظر شرط معنى بدليل إن كان علم الله قدومه ، في الموت لأنه كائن فلو عرف الشهر وقع بأوله كقبل الفطر فينزل قبيل الموت من أول الشهر توسيطاً بين الظهور الاستناد والاقتصار، فإذا قال لامرأته أنت طالق ثلاثاً قبل موت زيد بشهر ثم خلعها بعد خمسة عشر يوماً على ألف أو قال لعبده أنت حر قبل موت زيد بشهر ثم كاتبه على ألف بعد خمسة عشر يوماً ثم مات زيد بعد ذلك إلى وقت لم يتعلق من حق الوارث به لكن هذا لو الإيجاب في الصحة وإلا فمن الثلث اجماعاً، وللمولى. بيع العبد قبل مضي الشهر، وكذا بعده عنده لأنه لم يصر بذلك مدبراً مطلقاً لاشتراط القبلية وهي صفة زائدة فصار كقوله إن مت من مرضي هذا. ولو جنى على العبد بأن قطعت يده في الشهر ثم مات المولى لتمام الشهر فالأرش للعبد لا المولى لكن على القاطع أرش القن وهو نصف القيمة لا الحر وهو نصف الدية لأن العتق عنده ثبت مستنداً ولا استناد في الجزء الفائت وهو اليد والأرش، الخلف يعطي حكم الأصل عندهما
And among the branches of adding [a time]: 'You are divorced one month before the arrival of Zaid,' and similar. He said in al-Talkhis, chapter on what occurs by time and what does not: 'You are divorced three times one month before I marry you' is meaningless because the contract precedes it, like 'you were divorced yesterday' said to a woman he marries today. He affirmed that the speech extends over a long time. His statement: 'Hence it was said in al-Zahiriyyah...' i.e., his saying 'I will not speak to you today' since the 'al' is for the present reference, it is confined to the whiteness of the present day, so if he speaks to her after that at night, he does not break his oath, unlike the second issue because it is like 'I will not speak to you for three days' including the night. In al-Nahr: if the first branch is based on the speech being extended, it would be independent of this restriction. And what the author said is more apparent because it necessitates restriction to the whiteness of the day, even if it is said that the speech is not extended, contrary to what is said in al-Nahr, for it would necessitate no restriction according to the other view, while 'today' is defined by the present reference, so how can it include other than it? Ponder. His statement: 'meaningless because the contract precedes it' means that his saying that to a non-wife is meaningless, no ruling attaches to it, so that if he later marries her, she is never divorced: either because the contract precedes if the contract occurs before a month from that statement, as in 'you were divorced yesterday' to someone he marries today; or because the contract coincides if a full month or more passes from the time of that statement. This is because divorce depends on the existence of marriage, not because it is a condition but because it is a place of consumption for the condition which is the month connected to the marriage, since he uttered divorce one month before, at the end of which he marries, so the month is a condition known by the first time of marriage, so its existence is just before marriage, so the conditioned, which is divorce, occurs after the month coinciding with the marriage. But divorce in law is a raiser of marriage, so it cannot coincide with it, nor is it a verbal condition entering upon marriage in his speech so that the occurrence of divorce is delayed after the marriage, as in his saying 'if I marry you, you are divorced one month before it,' and he marries after one month. As for his saying to his wife 'you are divorced one month before the arrival of Zaid' or 'one month before his death,' it occurs if they happen after one month, because of the addition and description within ownership, where he added the divorce of his married wife to a month described with a description which is the arrival or death, and it has occurred while the woman is in his ownership. And his statement 'confined' (muqtasiran) is a circumstantial clause from the pronoun in 'occurs' i.e., occurs confined according to the two companions to the time of the arrival or death, because each is a condition for the suspension of divorce upon it; while according to Zufar it is based (mustanidan) because of the addition of divorce to the described time, which is a month at the end of which is Zaid's arrival or death. So when it occurs, it becomes clear that the month was described from its beginning with this description, so the waiting period is counted from its beginning. And emancipation has this same disagreement. Imam is with them in the matter of arrival, so he effects divorce and emancipation as confined because arrival is a definer of the condition, and the definer, if it is at risk of existence, is a condition in meaning even if its letter is not mentioned, or its coincidence, for it is suspended for identification, and it is not a verbal condition to delay. And 'one month before the arrival of Zaid or his death' occurs if they are after one month with it, because of the addition and description within ownership, confined according to them for suspension, based according to Zufar because of the addition. Similarly in emancipation. Imam is with them in the matter of arrival because the definer of risk is a condition in meaning, as evidenced by if he says 'if in God's knowledge Zaid will arrive in a month, you are divorced' and he arrives at its completion, she is divorced after his arrival confined. But since the arrival is not known to us, the ruling is suspended on its appearance to us, and it becomes in the meaning of a condition. And with Zufar in the matter of death, he effects both as based because it is inevitably occurring, so it is not in the meaning of a condition; thus it is a definer of the time to which divorce is added, which is the month. So when the month is known, divorce occurs at its beginning, as in the originally known month in his saying 'you are divorced one month before al-Fitr.' And knowledge of the month in our issue is realized by the appearance of the signs of death; so the definer that it is a month before Zaid's death is those signs, not death itself, so it does not have the ruling of a condition in terms of meaning, unlike arrival. Thus death at the beginning is a revealer of the month, and at the end is a condition for suspension of its existence upon it, so it oscillates between manifestation and initiation. So we establish a ruling between them: that divorce descends just before death upon the appearance of signs, based on the beginning of the month, as a middle way between them, to act upon both. As summarized in Sharh al-Farisi. His statement: 'until the khul' and kitabah become void' is a branch on the disagreement between Imam and his two companions regarding istinad and iqtisar. So if he says to his wife 'you are divorced three times one month before Zaid's death,' then he makes khul' with her after fifteen days for one thousand, or if he says to his slave 'you are free one month before Zaid's death,' then he makes kitabah with him for one thousand after fifteen days, then Zaid dies after that at the completion of one month, the khul' and kitabah are void according to him because of the precedence of the removal of the subject matter, so the husband returns the dower of khul' and the master returns the kitabah price, except if Zaid dies after the expiry of the waiting period and the payment of the mukatib. And the suspended divorce with a month before the husband's death is void according to them because of its coincidence with the removal of the ownership of marriage, and divorce added to a state of removal of marriage is invalid. According to him, it occurs at the appearance of signs of death because the subject matter exists, then it is based. And his statement: 'unlike emancipation' means that in 'you are free one month before my death,' emancipation occurs by agreement. As for according to him, it is apparent; as for according to them, it is because ownership remains after death if the deceased is in need of it. Hence if he says 'you are free one month after my death,' it is valid, and it is not an addition to a state of removal of ownership, but he becomes free from one-third because it is confined to death, so he is like a mudabbar. According to him, he becomes free from the whole because it is based on a time that has no connection to the heir's right, but this is if the contract is made during health; otherwise, it is from one-third by consensus. And the master may sell the slave before the month elapses, and similarly after it according to him because he has not thereby become a mudabbar absolutely due to the condition of priority, which is an additional quality, so it becomes like his saying 'if I die from this illness.' And if someone injures the slave by cutting off his hand during the month, then the master dies at the completion of the month, the compensation is for the slave, not the master, but the injurer must pay the compensation of a slave (half the value) not a free man (half the blood money), because according to him emancipation is established as based, and there is no basing in the missing part which is the hand and its compensation; the later ruling gives the ruling of the original according to them.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage presents one of the most important intra-Hanafi disputes concerning the timing of conditional divorce. The issue arises when a husband says to his wife, 'You are divorced one month before Zaid's arrival (or death).' The key question is: at what exact moment does the divorce take effect? Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) differ, with Zufar also holding a distinct view.

The text begins by distinguishing between saying this to an ajnabiyya (non-wife) versus to one's wife. If said to a non-wife, it is لغو (meaningless) because the marriage is not yet in place. The divorce is conditioned on the marriage occurring within a month; if marriage occurs after a month, it coincides with the divorce, which is invalid since divorce cannot coincide with marriage. If marriage occurs before a month, the divorce is even more impossible.

When said to one's wife, the ruling depends on whether the specified event (arrival or death) is considered a true condition (shart) or a mere identifier (mu'arraf) for the time. According to the Sahibayn (and also in one narration from Abu Hanifa regarding arrival), the divorce occurs only at the moment of the event (iqtisar) because the event is a condition upon which the divorce depends. The month merely defines the timeframe. So if Zaid arrives, the wife is divorced at that moment, and the 'iddah begins from then. Zufar, however, argues that the divorce is based (mustanid) from the beginning of the month because the addition of divorce to a described time (a month at the end of which is the event) makes the divorce effective from the start of that month. The waiting period would then begin from the start of the month.

Imam Abu Hanifa differentiates between arrival and death. Arrival is a contingent event—it may or may not happen—so it is in the meaning of a condition (shart ma'nawi), hence the divorce is confined (muqtasir) to the moment of arrival. Death, however, is inevitable; it is not a condition but a definer of the month. Therefore, in the case of death, the month is known (by signs of death), so the divorce is based (mustanid) from the beginning of the month. This is a middle position: the divorce descends just before death (at the appearance of signs) but is considered effective from the first of the month, to honor both the idea of condition and the definitive nature of death.

The practical consequences (thamarah) are significant: If the husband makes khul' or kitabah during the conditional period, according to Imam Abu Hanifa these are void because the subject matter (the marriage or slavery) has already been effectively removed by the retroactive divorce from the beginning of the month. According to the Sahibayn, since the divorce occurs only at the later event, the khul' and kitabah are valid and then the divorce occurs later. The text discusses the return of dower, the effect on emancipation, and the case of injury to a slave.

This dispute is a hallmark of Hanafi legal theory, showcasing the school's sophisticated use of linguistic interpretation and conceptual analysis (tahlil al-ma'na). The reliance on the nature of the event—whether it is a true condition or a definer—drives the legal ruling.

Key Terms
لغو (laghw): Legally meaningless; no ruling attaches.
سبق العقد (sabq al-'aqd): The contract (marriage) precedes the divorce statement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling when a man says to a non-wife 'You are divorced one month before Zaid's arrival'?
A) She is divorced when Zaid arrives if marriage occurs before.
B) She is divorced immediately upon his saying it.
C) The statement is meaningless (لغو), she is never divorced.
D) She is divorced if she marries him within one month.

Key Takeaway
A conditional divorce before a future event is invalid if the marriage does not exist at the time of the statement.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
12 min
Conditional Divorce to a Wife: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Istinad vs Iqtisar
Intra-Hanafi dispute on conditional divorce timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, the Two Companions, and Zufar regarding the timing of a conditional divorce said to a wife, and apply this to practical consequences like khul and 'iddah.

Core Idea
Whether a conditional divorce is retroactive (istinad) or confined to the event (iqtisar) depends on whether the specified event is contingent or inevitable.

When a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced one month before Zaid's arrival (or death),' the Hanafi school is divided on when exactly the divorce takes effect. The Two Companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Hanifa on arrival hold that the divorce occurs only at the moment of the event (iqtisar). Zufar argues that it is effective from the beginning of the month (istinad). Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes between arrival (contingent) and death (inevitable), adopting istinad for the latter. This dispute has significant practical effects on khul', kitabah, emancipation, and the start of 'iddah. The passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains these positions and their consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement and the parties
The husband says to his wife 'You are divorced one month before Zaid's arrival' or 'one month before his death.' The wife is in his ownership at the time.
2
Understand the two concepts: istinad and iqtisar
Istinad means the divorce is effective retroactively from the beginning of the month. Iqtisar means the divorce occurs only at the moment the event (arrival/death) occurs.
3
Analyze the positions based on the nature of the event
Zufar applies istinad for both arrival and death because the month is described by the event; thus the divorce attaches to the month. The Sahibayn apply iqtisar for both because the event is a condition. Imam Abu Hanifa adopts iqtisar for arrival (contingent) and istinad for death (inevitable).
Imam's rationale: arrival is uncertain (condition in meaning), death is certain (definer).
4
Apply the views to branches
Consider khul' or kitabah performed before the event. Under iqtisar, they are valid because the marriage/slavery still exists. Under istinad, they are void because the divorce/slave emancipation was retroactive, removing the subject matter.
Also consider 'iddah start and compensation in case of injury.

. كذا في العتق والإمام معهما في القدوم إذ المعرف الحظر شرط معنى بدليل إن كان علم الله قدومه ، في الموت لأنه كائن فلو عرف الشهر وقع بأوله كقبل الفطر فينزل قبيل الموت من أول الشهر توسيطاً بين الظهور والإنشاء حتى لغا الخلع، والكتابة عنده سبق الزوال فيرد البدل إلا يموت بعد العدة لفوت محل الإنشاء ولغا طالق قبل موتي بشهر عندهما لقران الموت أن بدليل ما لو قال إن كان في علم الله قدوم زيد إلى شهر فأنت طالق وقدم لتمامه فإنها تطلق بعد قدومه مقتصراً لكن لما لم يكن القدوم معلوماً لنا توقف الحكم على ظهوره لنا، وصار في معنى الشرط، ومع زفر في مسألة الموت فأوقعهما مستنداً لأنه كائن لا محالة فلم يكن في معنى الشرط فيكون معرفاً للوقت المضاف إليه الطلاق وهو الشهر، فإذا عرف الشهر وقع الطلاق بأوله كما في الشهر المعلوم من الأصل في قوله أنت طالق قبل الفطر بشهر ومعرفة الشهر في مسألتنا تتحقق بظهور آثار الموت فصار المعرف لكونه شهراً قبل موت زيد تلك الآثار لا الموت نفسه فلم يكن له حكم الشرط من حيث المعنى بخلاف القدوم فصار الموت في الابتداء مظهراً للشهر وفي الانتهاء شرطاً لتوقف وجوده عليه فدار بين الظهور والإنشاء فأثبتنا حكماً بينهما وهو نزول الطلاق قبيل الموت عند وجود الآثار مستنداً إلى أول الشهر توسيطاً بينهما عملاً بهما. كذا في شرح الفارسي ملخصاً قوله (حتى لغا الخ) تفريع على الاختلاف بين الإمام وصاحبيه في الاستناد والاقتصار، فإذا قال لامرأته أنت طالق ثلاثاً قبل موت زيد بشهر ثم خلعها بعد خمسة عشر يوماً على ألف أو قال لعبده أنت حر قبل موت زيد بشهر ثم كاتبه على ألف بعد خمسة عشر يوماً ثم مات زيد بعد ذلك لتمام شهر بطل الخلع والكتابة عنده لسبق زوال المحل فيرد الزوج بدل الخلع والمولى بدل الكتابة إلا أن يموت زيد بعد انقضاء العدة وأداء المكاتب ولغا الطلاق المعلق بشهر قبل موت الزوج عندهما لقرانه لزوال ملك النكاح والطلاق المضاف إلى حال زوال النكاح غير صحيح، وعنده يقع حين ظهور آثار الموت لقيام المحل ثم يستند، وقوله بخلاف العتق يعني في أنت حر قبل موتي بشهر حيث يقع العتاق اتفاقاً، أما عنده فظاهر وأما عندهما فلبقاء الملك بعد الموت إذا كان الميت محتاجاً إليه ولهذا إذا قال أنت حر بعد موتي بشهر صح فلم يكن إضافة إلى حال زوال الملك لكن يعتق الثلث لاقتصاره على الموت فكان كالمدبر وعنده من الكل لاستناده إلى وقت لم يتعلق من حق الوارث به لكن هذا لو الإيجاب في الصحة وإلا فمن الثلث اجماعاً، وللمولى. بيع العبد قبل مضي الشهر، وكذا بعده عنده لأنه لم يصر بذلك مدبراً مطلقاً لاشتراط القبلية وهي صفة زائدة فصار كقوله إن مت من مرضي هذا. ولو جنى على العبد بأن قطعت يده في الشهر ثم مات المولى لتمام الشهر فالأرش للعبد لا المولى لكن على القاطع أرش القن وهو نصف القيمة لا الحر وهو نصف الدية لأن العتق عنده ثبت مستنداً ولا استناد في الجزء الفائت وهو اليد والأرش، الخلف يعطي حكم الأصل عندهما
And among the branches of adding [a time]: 'You are divorced one month before the arrival of Zaid,' and similar. He said in al-Talkhis, chapter on what occurs by time and what does not: 'You are divorced three times one month before I marry you' is meaningless because the contract precedes it, like 'you were divorced yesterday' said to a woman he marries today. He affirmed that the speech extends over a long time. His statement: 'Hence it was said in al-Zahiriyyah...' i.e., his saying 'I will not speak to you today' since the 'al' is for the present reference, it is confined to the whiteness of the present day, so if he speaks to her after that at night, he does not break his oath, unlike the second issue because it is like 'I will not speak to you for three days' including the night. In al-Nahr: if the first branch is based on the speech being extended, it would be independent of this restriction. And what the author said is more apparent because it necessitates restriction to the whiteness of the day, even if it is said that the speech is not extended, contrary to what is said in al-Nahr, for it would necessitate no restriction according to the other view, while 'today' is defined by the present reference, so how can it include other than it? Ponder. His statement: 'meaningless because the contract precedes it' means that his saying that to a non-wife is meaningless, no ruling attaches to it, so that if he later marries her, she is never divorced: either because the contract precedes if the contract occurs before a month from that statement, as in 'you were divorced yesterday' to someone he marries today; or because the contract coincides if a full month or more passes from the time of that statement. This is because divorce depends on the existence of marriage, not because it is a condition but because it is a place of consumption for the condition which is the month connected to the marriage, since he uttered divorce one month before, at the end of which he marries, so the month is a condition known by the first time of marriage, so its existence is just before marriage, so the conditioned, which is divorce, occurs after the month coinciding with the marriage. But divorce in law is a raiser of marriage, so it cannot coincide with it, nor is it a verbal condition entering upon marriage in his speech so that the occurrence of divorce is delayed after the marriage, as in his saying 'if I marry you, you are divorced one month before it,' and he marries after one month. As for his saying to his wife 'you are divorced one month before the arrival of Zaid' or 'one month before his death,' it occurs if they happen after one month, because of the addition and description within ownership, where he added the divorce of his married wife to a month described with a description which is the arrival or death, and it has occurred while the woman is in his ownership. And his statement 'confined' (muqtasiran) is a circumstantial clause from the pronoun in 'occurs' i.e., occurs confined according to the two companions to the time of the arrival or death, because each is a condition for the suspension of divorce upon it; while according to Zufar it is based (mustanidan) because of the addition of divorce to the described time, which is a month at the end of which is Zaid's arrival or death. So when it occurs, it becomes clear that the month was described from its beginning with this description, so the waiting period is counted from its beginning. And emancipation has this same disagreement. Imam is with them in the matter of arrival, so he effects divorce and emancipation as confined because arrival is a definer of the condition, and the definer, if it is at risk of existence, is a condition in meaning even if its letter is not mentioned, or its coincidence, for it is suspended for identification, and it is not a verbal condition to delay. And 'one month before the arrival of Zaid or his death' occurs if they are after one month with it, because of the addition and description within ownership, confined according to them for suspension, based according to Zufar because of the addition. Similarly in emancipation. Imam is with them in the matter of arrival because the definer of risk is a condition in meaning, as evidenced by if he says 'if in God's knowledge Zaid will arrive in a month, you are divorced' and he arrives at its completion, she is divorced after his arrival confined. But since the arrival is not known to us, the ruling is suspended on its appearance to us, and it becomes in the meaning of a condition. And with Zufar in the matter of death, he effects both as based because it is inevitably occurring, so it is not in the meaning of a condition; thus it is a definer of the time to which divorce is added, which is the month. So when the month is known, divorce occurs at its beginning, as in the originally known month in his saying 'you are divorced one month before al-Fitr.' And knowledge of the month in our issue is realized by the appearance of the signs of death; so the definer that it is a month before Zaid's death is those signs, not death itself, so it does not have the ruling of a condition in terms of meaning, unlike arrival. Thus death at the beginning is a revealer of the month, and at the end is a condition for suspension of its existence upon it, so it oscillates between manifestation and initiation. So we establish a ruling between them: that divorce descends just before death upon the appearance of signs, based on the beginning of the month, as a middle way between them, to act upon both. As summarized in Sharh al-Farisi. His statement: 'until the khul' and kitabah become void' is a branch on the disagreement between Imam and his two companions regarding istinad and iqtisar. So if he says to his wife 'you are divorced three times one month before Zaid's death,' then he makes khul' with her after fifteen days for one thousand, or if he says to his slave 'you are free one month before Zaid's death,' then he makes kitabah with him for one thousand after fifteen days, then Zaid dies after that at the completion of one month, the khul' and kitabah are void according to him because of the precedence of the removal of the subject matter, so the husband returns the dower of khul' and the master returns the kitabah price, except if Zaid dies after the expiry of the waiting period and the payment of the mukatib. And the suspended divorce with a month before the husband's death is void according to them because of its coincidence with the removal of the ownership of marriage, and divorce added to a state of removal of marriage is invalid. According to him, it occurs at the appearance of signs of death because the subject matter exists, then it is based. And his statement: 'unlike emancipation' means that in 'you are free one month before my death,' emancipation occurs by agreement. As for according to him, it is apparent; as for according to them, it is because ownership remains after death if the deceased is in need of it. Hence if he says 'you are free one month after my death,' it is valid, and it is not an addition to a state of removal of ownership, but he becomes free from one-third because it is confined to death, so he is like a mudabbar. According to him, he becomes free from the whole because it is based on a time that has no connection to the heir's right, but this is if the contract is made during health; otherwise, it is from one-third by consensus. And the master may sell the slave before the month elapses, and similarly after it according to him because he has not thereby become a mudabbar absolutely due to the condition of priority, which is an additional quality, so it becomes like his saying 'if I die from this illness.' And if someone injures the slave by cutting off his hand during the month, then the master dies at the completion of the month, the compensation is for the slave, not the master, but the injurer must pay the compensation of a slave (half the value) not a free man (half the blood money), because according to him emancipation is established as based, and there is no basing in the missing part which is the hand and its compensation; the later ruling gives the ruling of the original according to them.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage presents one of the most important intra-Hanafi disputes concerning the timing of conditional divorce. The issue arises when a husband says to his wife, 'You are divorced one month before Zaid's arrival (or death).' The key question is: at what exact moment does the divorce take effect? Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) differ, with Zufar also holding a distinct view.

The text begins by distinguishing between saying this to an ajnabiyya (non-wife) versus to one's wife. If said to a non-wife, it is لغو (meaningless) because the marriage is not yet in place. The divorce is conditioned on the marriage occurring within a month; if marriage occurs after a month, it coincides with the divorce, which is invalid since divorce cannot coincide with marriage. If marriage occurs before a month, the divorce is even more impossible.

When said to one's wife, the ruling depends on whether the specified event (arrival or death) is considered a true condition (shart) or a mere identifier (mu'arraf) for the time. According to the Sahibayn (and also in one narration from Abu Hanifa regarding arrival), the divorce occurs only at the moment of the event (iqtisar) because the event is a condition upon which the divorce depends. The month merely defines the timeframe. So if Zaid arrives, the wife is divorced at that moment, and the 'iddah begins from then. Zufar, however, argues that the divorce is based (mustanid) from the beginning of the month because the addition of divorce to a described time (a month at the end of which is the event) makes the divorce effective from the start of that month. The waiting period would then begin from the start of the month.

Imam Abu Hanifa differentiates between arrival and death. Arrival is a contingent event—it may or may not happen—so it is in the meaning of a condition (shart ma'nawi), hence the divorce is confined (muqtasir) to the moment of arrival. Death, however, is inevitable; it is not a condition but a definer of the month. Therefore, in the case of death, the month is known (by signs of death), so the divorce is based (mustanid) from the beginning of the month. This is a middle position: the divorce descends just before death (at the appearance of signs) but is considered effective from the first of the month, to honor both the idea of condition and the definitive nature of death.

The practical consequences (thamarah) are significant: If the husband makes khul' or kitabah during the conditional period, according to Imam Abu Hanifa these are void because the subject matter (the marriage or slavery) has already been effectively removed by the retroactive divorce from the beginning of the month. According to the Sahibayn, since the divorce occurs only at the later event, the khul' and kitabah are valid and then the divorce occurs later. The text discusses the return of dower, the effect on emancipation, and the case of injury to a slave.

This dispute is a hallmark of Hanafi legal theory, showcasing the school's sophisticated use of linguistic interpretation and conceptual analysis (tahlil al-ma'na). The reliance on the nature of the event—whether it is a true condition or a definer—drives the legal ruling.

Key Terms
استناد (istinad): Retroactive effect from the beginning of the month.
اقتصار (iqtisar): Confinement of the divorce to the moment of the event.
شرط معنوي (shart ma'nawi): A condition in meaning, not verbal; the event functions as a condition because it is contingent.
معرف (mu'arraf): A definer that identifies the time without being a condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, when does the divorce take effect if a husband says 'You are divorced one month before my death' and he dies after one month?
A) At the moment of death.
B) At the beginning of the month, retroactively.
C) At the middle of the month.
D) It does not take effect because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the timing of a conditional divorce depends on whether the specified event is contingent (iqtisar) or inevitable (istinad).

Istinad vs Iqtisar: The Internal Hanafi Dispute on Suspended Divorce
Explains the difference between retroactive effect and limitation when divorce is suspended before a condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding retroactive effect (istinad) and limitation (iqtisar) in suspended divorce, and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When divorce is tied to a certain event like death, it takes effect retroactively; when tied to an uncertain event, it is limited to the moment of occurrence.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines a nuanced dispute within the Hanafi school about the timing of a divorce that is suspended by a phrase like 'before the death of Zaid by a month.' The key question is whether the divorce takes effect from the beginning of the month (istinad) or only at the moment of death (iqtisar). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly determining the onset of the 'idda and the validity of subsequent contracts like khul' and kitaba.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa (the Imam) rules for divorce suspended before death. He says istinad (retroactive) because death is certain.
This is the majority position within the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing view
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). They say iqtisar (limitation) – the divorce only occurs at the moment of death.
They argue that the month is not known with certainty.
3
Understand Zufar's position
Zufar says istinad for both death and arrival, making him an outlier.
Zufar's view is noted but not relied upon.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Why does Abu Hanifa treat death differently from arrival? Because death is inevitable, so the condition is more like an identifier of the month, not a true condition.
The signs of death manifest the month.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if the husband dies before the month ends, according to Abu Hanifa the divorce occurs retroactively, so 'idda starts from the beginning of the month; according to the Sahibayn, no divorce occurs.
This affects the validity of khul' and kitaba done during that period.

So if he said to his wife: 'You are divorced thrice before the death of Zaid by a month,' then he made khul' with her after fifteen days for one thousand, or he said to his slave: 'You are free before the death of Zaid by a month,' then he made kitaba for one thousand after fifteen days, then Zaid died after that at the completion of the month, the khul' and kitaba become void according to him due to prior loss of the place, so the husband returns the compensation of khul' and the master returns the compensation of kitaba, unless Zaid dies after the expiration of the 'idda and the payment of the makatib. And the divorce suspended by a month before the husband's death becomes void according to them due to its conjunction with death because the ownership of marriage ceases, and divorce added to a state of cessation of ownership is invalid. According to him, it occurs at the appearance of the signs of death due to the existence of the place, then it becomes based.

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the ruling when a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced before the death of Zaid by a month' or 'before the arrival of Zaid by a month.' The key issue is whether the divorce takes effect retroactively (istinad) from the beginning of the month or only at the moment the condition is realized (iqtisar). Abu Hanifa holds that when the condition is death (which is certain), the divorce is istinad – it occurs at the beginning of the month because the month is known through signs of death, and death itself is not a condition but an identifier. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it is iqtisar – the divorce occurs only at the moment of death, but it is limited to that point. Zufar takes a middle position. The passage then applies this difference to khul' and kitaba: if the condition fails (e.g., the husband dies before the month ends), the khul' or kitaba becomes void according to Abu Hanifa because the place of initiation is lost, but according to the two disciples, the divorce is void because it would be added to a state where ownership no longer exists. The text explains the reasoning and concludes that Abu Hanifa's position is based on the certainty of death.

Key Terms
استناد (istinād): Retroactive effect; the divorce is considered to have occurred from the beginning of the month even though the condition (death) is fulfilled later.
اقتصار (iqtisār): Limitation; the divorce only takes effect at the moment the condition is fulfilled, not retroactively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) At the moment of Zaid's death.
C) Only after the wife completes her idda.
D) It does not take effect because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
When a divorce is suspended 'before death by a month,' Abu Hanifa's position of retroactive effect (istinad) is the relied-upon view, and it applies only to certain events like death, not uncertain ones like arrival.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Suspended Emancipation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on retroactive emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the retroactive effect of suspended emancipation and apply the thamarah al-khilaf to determine the slave's share of the estate.

Core Idea
Emancipation suspended before death is valid, but does it free the whole slave or just one-third? Abu Hanifa says whole; Sahibayn say one-third.

In this passage, the author compares suspended emancipation (mudabbar) to divorce. While all agree that saying 'you are free before my death by a month' results in emancipation, the extent of freedom and when it takes effect is disputed. Abu Hanifa argues that the emancipation is retroactive to the beginning of the month, freeing the slave from the entire estate if the master was in health. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, limit the freedom to one-third of the estate, treating it as a bequest. We will explore the proof for each and the practical consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The master says 'you are free before my death by a month.' The emancipation is suspended until death. All agreed that emancipation occurs at some point.
The condition is the death occurring after a month from the pronouncement.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that the slave is free from the entire estate because the emancipation is retroactive (istinad) to the beginning of the month. The slave is considered free from the moment of pronouncement in terms of ownership, so the heirs have no claim.
The proof is that ownership continues after death for burial needs, so adding emancipation to that period is not adding to a state of loss of ownership.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's position
The two disciples hold that the slave is free only from one-third of the estate. They argue that death terminates ownership, so the emancipation is like a bequest (wasiyya) and limited to one-third.
They treat the slave as a mudabbar (promised freedom at death) which is always from one-third.
4
Identify the consensus exception
If the pronouncement is made in sickness (marad al-mawt), then all agree it is from one-third only. The dispute only applies when the master is in health.
This is a crucial boundary: the full retroactive effect only applies in health.
5
Determine the practical difference
In health: according to Abu Hanifa, the slave is fully free from the entire estate, so heirs cannot claim him. According to Sahibayn, only one-third of the slave's value goes to freedom, the rest belongs to the estate. In sickness: both agree on one-third.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the distribution of the slave's value among heirs.

And his statement: contrary to emancipation, meaning in 'you are free before my death by a month' where emancipation occurs by agreement. As for him (Abu Hanifa) it is apparent; as for them (the two disciples) because ownership remains after death if the deceased needs it. Hence, if he says 'you are free after my death by a month' it is valid, so it is not an addition to a state of loss of ownership, but he becomes free from one-third due to limitation to death, so he is like a mudabbar. According to him, from the whole because it is based on a time not attached to the heir's right, but this is if the pronouncement is in health; otherwise from one-third by consensus. And the master may sell the slave before the month passes, and likewise after according to him because he does not thereby become a mudabbar absolutely due to the condition of priority which is an extra attribute, so it becomes like his saying 'if I die from this illness.' And if someone injures the slave by cutting off his hand during the month, then the master dies at the end of the month, the blood money is for the slave not the master, but on the cutter is the blood money of a slave which is half the value, not of a free man which is half the diya, because emancipation according to him is established retroactively, and there is no retroactivity in the lost part which is the hand and the blood money. The substitute takes the ruling of the original according to them, contrary to emancipation due to the remaining of ownership, but from one-third according to them and the whole according to him, and he may sell with a condition of death or other with it like 'if I die and am buried' or 'from my illness.' And if someone injures him in the month, the blood money is for him but the blood money of a slave since there is no retroactivity in the lost part and the substitute is like the original in that which it accepts, which is ownership, not emancipation. Its analogy is the injury on the sa'i in the kitaba of his father, and the liability of causation attaches to the deceased after the heir's emancipation, for it is in a right that accepts it, which is the slave's entitlement from the beginning of the month, not that which does not accept it, which is emancipation. And its analogy is the ruling on injury on the son who is a sa'i in his father's kitaba after the father's death: if his hand is cut off, then he pays and it is judged that he and his father are free at the end of the father's life, the blood money is for him as a slave, not as a free man, because the substitute (blood money) is like the original (hand) in that which accepts it (ownership for the son) not that which does not accept it (freedom). Similarly, liability of causation: if the testator digs a well in the road, then dies leaving a slave, and the heir frees him, then an animal worth the slave is destroyed by the well, the liability attaches to the digging in that which accepts it (debt on the deceased) so that the heir guarantees the slave's value, not in that which does not accept it (reversing the emancipation). This is according to him; according to them, half the value is due to the master because the cutting occurred on his ownership due to limitation. And his statement: 'and if he sells half' i.e. if the master sells half, then Zaid dies at the end of the month, the remaining half becomes free by consensus. And his statement: 'and it is not corrupted' is a response to what might be said: if the remaining becomes free retroactively, it appears that he is partially free, so he is a makatib and his sale is not allowed. The answer: the master did not make him a makatib explicitly, so if kitaba becomes apparent, it appears necessarily due to the freeing of half, so it is limited to that extent, and the necessity is in establishing freedom in his share, not in making the other a makatib. The buyer does not guarantee anything for the half because the freedom is established without his action, as it is established by the previous speech on the buyer's ownership, just as if he inherited half of someone who becomes free by kinship. All of this.

Commentary
This passage compares the previous ruling on divorce with emancipation ('itq). When a master says 'you are free before my death by a month,' all agree emancipation occurs, but the difference is in its retroactive effect and share of the estate. Abu Hanifa holds that the slave is free from the beginning of the month and thus from the entire estate (if in health). The two disciples hold that the slave becomes free only from one-third of the estate because death is a limiting condition. The passage then discusses the master's right to sell the slave during the month, injury to the slave, and analogies to other situations like the sa'i (striving slave) in kitaba and liability for a well. The principle is that the substitute (blood money or compensation) takes the ruling of the original in matters that accept retroactivity (ownership) but not in matters that do not (emancipation).

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is promised freedom upon the master's death, typically a form of bequest.
ساعي (sāʿī): A slave who is allowed to earn and pay for his freedom under kitaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One-third.
B) The entire slave.
C) Half.
D) None, because the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In suspended emancipation, Abu Hanifa holds full retroactive freedom from the whole estate in health, while the two disciples limit it to one-third; the position in sickness is unified on one-third.

Legal Outcomes and Analogies for the Mudabbar Slave
Legal outcomes and qiyas for mudabbar slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of qiyas khafi to deduce rulings on injury, sale, and compensation for a mudabbar slave and explain how the substitute takes the ruling of the original in matters of ownership but not emancipation.

Core Idea
When a conditional emancipation is pending, the master can still sell, and compensation for injury goes to the slave but computed as a slave, not free, because retroactivity does not apply to lost parts.

This passage continues the discussion on the mudabbar slave, now exploring practical issues: can the master sell him? What if someone injures him during the period? How is compensation calculated? The author uses a powerful tool of qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) to compare these cases to other scenarios like a sa'i in kitaba or a well digger's liability. The key principle is that the substitute (e.g., blood money) takes the ruling of the original (the hand) in matters that accept retroactivity, i.e., ownership, but not in matters that do not, i.e., freedom.

Guided Path
1
Rule on sale of the mudabbar during the period
The master may sell the slave before or after the month according to Abu Hanifa because the condition of priority (qabliyya) is an extra attribute, so the slave does not become a mudabbar absolutely. The sale is valid.
The sale after the month is also valid because the emancipation is retroactive, so the slave was technically free at the time of sale? Actually, Abu Hanifa allows sale even after the month because the slave is not fully free until death.
2
Injury to the slave during the month
If the slave's hand is cut, then the master dies at the month's end, the blood money goes to the slave (not the master) according to Abu Hanifa, but it is calculated as a slave's blood money (half the value of the slave), not as a free person's diya. This is because the lost part (hand) was lost when the slave was still a slave, and retroactivity does not apply to the lost part.
The principle: 'no retroactivity in the lost part.'
3
The principle of istinad and the substitute
The compensation (substitute) takes the ruling of the original (the hand) in that which it accepts (ownership) but not in that which it does not accept (emancipation). The ownership over the hand at the time of injury belonged to the master, but because the slave ultimately becomes free, the compensation goes to the slave, but the value is based on slave status.
This is a key qiyas khafi: the substitute is analogous to the original in some respects but not all.
4
Analogous cases: sa'i in kitaba and well liability
The same principle applies to a sa'i (striving slave) in kitaba: if he is injured before becoming free, his compensation is as a slave. Similarly, if a testator digs a well and the heir frees a slave, then an animal falls into the well, the liability attaches to the digger's estate for the slave's value, but the emancipation is not reversed.
These analogies show the consistent application of the rule across different contexts.
5
Clarification on selling half and kitaba appearance
If the master sells half of the slave, then the condition is fulfilled and the remaining half becomes free. This does not make the slave a makatib (contract slave) because the master did not explicitly make a kitaba contract. The buyer does not guarantee anything for the half because the freedom is established by the prior condition.
This resolves a potential objection about partial freedom.

And his statement: contrary to emancipation, meaning in 'you are free before my death by a month' where emancipation occurs by agreement. As for him (Abu Hanifa) it is apparent; as for them (the two disciples) because ownership remains after death if the deceased needs it. This is according to him; according to them, half the value is due to the master because the cutting occurred on his ownership due to limitation. And his statement: 'and if he sells half' i.e. if the master sells half, then Zaid dies at the end of the month, the remaining half becomes free by consensus. And his statement: 'and it is not corrupted' is a response to what might be said: if the remaining becomes free retroactively, it appears that he is partially free, so he is a makatib and his sale is not allowed. The answer: the master did not make him a makatib explicitly, so if kitaba becomes apparent, it appears necessarily due to the freeing of half, so it is limited to that extent, and the necessity is in establishing freedom in his share, not in making the other a makatib. The buyer does not guarantee anything for the half because the freedom is established without his action, as it is established by the previous speech on the buyer's ownership, just as if he inherited half of someone who becomes free by kinship. All of this.

Commentary
This passage compares the previous ruling on divorce with emancipation ('itq). When a master says 'you are free before my death by a month,' all agree emancipation occurs, but the difference is in its retroactive effect and share of the estate. Abu Hanifa holds that the slave is free from the beginning of the month and thus from the entire estate (if in health). The two disciples hold that the slave becomes free only from one-third of the estate because death is a limiting condition. The passage then discusses the master's right to sell the slave during the month, injury to the slave, and analogies to other situations like the sa'i (striving slave) in kitaba and liability for a well. The principle is that the substitute (blood money or compensation) takes the ruling of the original in matters that accept retroactivity (ownership) but not in matters that do not (emancipation).

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is promised freedom upon the master's death, typically a form of bequest.
ساعي (sāʿī): A slave who is allowed to earn and pay for his freedom under kitaba.
الخلف يأخذ حكم الأصل (al-khalaf ya'khudh hukm al-asl): The substitute takes the ruling of the original; a principle used in qiyas and fiqh.
