Suspended Divorce Before Death of Two Persons: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Discusses the ruling when divorce is suspended before the death of two individuals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on retroactivity when divorce is suspended before the death of two persons, and apply the distinction between certain and uncertain events.

Core Idea
When divorce is linked to two deaths, the first death determines the month because death is certain; no waiting for the second.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced scenario in suspended divorces: when a husband links divorce to the death of two individuals within a month. The core question is whether the divorce takes effect retroactively to the beginning of that month or only at the moment of the first death, and whether we wait for the second death. Abu Hanifa and his two disciples differ on retroactivity, and the key lies in the certainty of death versus uncertainty of arrival.

Guided Path
1
Define the Suspension Scenario
The husband says 'you are divorced before the death of Zaid and Amr by a month.' Understand the condition: the divorce is suspended until the death of both, but the month is measured from the first death.
The month is added to the first of the two events.
2
Distinguish the Two Hanafi Positions
Abu Hanifa: divorce occurs retroactively (istinad) to the beginning of the month at the death of the first. Sahibayn: divorce occurs at the moment of the first death but without retroactivity (iqtisar). Neither waits for the second death.
The dispute is over retroactivity, not timing.
3
Analyze the Distinction Between Death and Arrival
The text contrasts this with a similar condition involving arrival (qudum) of two persons. For arrival, the divorce does not occur until both arrive because the second may never arrive, so the condition is incomplete. Death is certain, so the second's death is irrelevant for the condition.
Certainty (yaqin) vs potential non-occurrence.
4
Identify the Thamarah al-Khilaf
According to Abu Hanifa, the wife's idda begins from the beginning of the month (retroactive). According to the Sahibayn, it begins from the moment of the first death. This affects her marriage and waiting period calculations.
Practical outcome differs in dates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله «ولو قال أي لو قال لامرأته أنت طالق قبل موت زيد وعمرو بشهر فمات أحدهما قبل شهر من وقت الكلام فات الوصف وهو القبلية على موتهما بشهر ففات الموصوف وهو الوقت المضاف إليه الطلاق فتعذر الوقوع، وإن مات أحدهما بعد شهر وقع مستنداً عنده إلى أول الشهر مقتصراً عندهما لا ينتظر موت الآخر لتعين الشهر المضاف إليه الطلاق وهو المتصل بأول الكائنين وهما موت زيد وعمرو لا محالة لأنه لم يبق للثاني تأثير في إيجاد الشرط فلا يتوقف عليه فصار كأنت طالق قبل الفطر والأضحى بشهر يقع في أول رمضان ولا ينتظر ما بعده، وهذا بخلاف القدوم في أنت طالق قبل قدوم زيد وعمرو بشهر لا يقع ما لم يقدم الآخر لعدم تعين الشهر المضاف إليه الطلاق عند اتصاله بأولهما لجواز أن لا يقدم الآخر أصلاً فكان للثاني تأثير في إيجاد الشرط، فإذا قدم طلقت بطريق الاقتصار خلافاً لزفر، أما في الموت فيتعين الشهر بموت أحدهما لكون موت الآخر كائناً لا محالة
And his statement: 'and if he said' i.e. if he said to his wife 'you are divorced before the death of Zaid and Amr by a month,' and one of them dies before a month from the time of speech, the attribute (prior to both deaths) is lost, so the described (time) is lost, so occurrence is impossible. If one of them dies after a month, it occurs retroactively according to him (Abu Hanifa) to the beginning of the month, but limited according to them (the two disciples), not waiting for the other's death, because the month added to the divorce is determined as the month connected to the first of the two events (deaths of Zaid and Amr) inevitably, since the second has no effect in creating the condition, so it does not wait. This becomes like 'you are divorced before al-Fitr and al-Adha by a month,' which occurs at the beginning of Ramadan and does not wait for what comes after. This is contrary to arrival: in 'you are divorced before the arrival of Zaid and Amr by a month,' it does not occur until the other arrives, because the month is not determined when connected to their arrival due to the possibility that the other may not arrive at all, so the second has an effect in creating the condition. So if he arrives, she is divorced by way of limitation, contrary to Zufar. As for death, the month is determined by the death of one because the other's death is inevitable.

Commentary
This passage addresses a more specific scenario: the husband says 'you are divorced before the death of Zaid and Amr by a month.' If both die, the ruling is as before. If only one dies after a month, the divorce takes effect retroactively according to Abu Hanifa (istinad) to the beginning of the month, but according to the two disciples, it is limited (iqtisar) to that moment. Importantly, they do not wait for the other's death because death is certain for both eventually. This contrasts with arrival where the second person may never arrive, so the divorce does not occur until both arrive. The analogy is made with 'before Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha by a month' where the month is determined by the first Eid. The key distinction is between certain events (death) and uncertain ones (arrival).

Key Terms
قران (qirān): Conjunction; here referring to the simultaneous occurrence of two conditions or events.
استناد (istinād): Retroactivity; the divorce is linked back to an earlier time.
اقتصار (iqtisār): Limitation; the divorce takes effect only at the moment of the first death without retroactive effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In suspended divorces, the certainty of an event determines whether retroactivity is applied; death is certain, so the first death triggers the divorce without waiting for the second.

Refuting al-Razi's Objection on Conjunction in Suspended Divorce
Refutes an objection by al-Razi on conjunction requirement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects the requirement of conjunction (qiran) in suspended divorce using the principle of istihsan.

Core Idea
Divorce suspended on two deaths takes effect at the first death because conjunction is impossible – istihsan overrides strict analogy.

This short passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a specific objection raised by al-Razi against the Hanafi ruling on suspended divorce. Al-Razi argued that by strict analogy the divorce should not occur unless both deaths happen simultaneously. The Hanafi response relies on istihsan, overriding analogy due to practical impossibility. Understanding this debate sharpens your grasp of how Hanafi jurists resolve conflicts between qiyas and custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed condition
The passage refers to a divorce suspended on the death of two persons. The condition states that the divorce occurs 'upon the death of both.' The key dispute is whether this requires their deaths to be conjoined (muqtarinan) in time.
The term 'quran' here means conjunction, not the sacred book.
2
State al-Razi's objection and his qiyas
Al-Razi argued by analogy (qiyas) that if the deaths are not simultaneous, the divorce would occur at a time not matching the stated condition. Therefore, he insisted on actual conjunction.
His argument is based on literal adherence to the condition wording.
3
Explain the Hanafi response
The Hanafi position, as presented in the text, declares that requiring conjunction is impossible by custom (muhal 'aadan). Because of this impossibility, the jurists apply istihsan (juridical preference) to allow the divorce to take effect at the first death.
Istihsan overrides qiyas when the analogy leads to an impractical or harmful result.
4
Recognize the practical consequence
Without istihsan, the condition would never be fulfilled, leaving the marriage in limbo. The Hanafi ruling brings certainty: the divorce occurs at the first death, which is a workable and rational outcome.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical difference between the two positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والقرآن) مبتدأ خبره قوله مبنى طعن الرازي وهو إشارة إلى أن القياس في الصورتين أنه لا يقع الطلاق ما لم يقترن موتهما أو قدومهما وهو الذي بنى عليه الرازي طعنه في هذه المسألة لأنه لو وقع بعد موت أحدهما بشهر وموت الآخر بأكثر كان خلاف الوقت المضاف إليه الطلاق وقوله (وهو) أي اشتراط قران موتهما أو قدومهما محال عادة
His statement: (and the Quran) is a subject, its predicate is his statement 'the foundation of al-Razi's objection,' and it is an indication that the analogy in both cases is that the divorce does not occur unless their deaths or arrivals are concurrent, which is what al-Razi based his objection on in this issue, because if it occurred after the death of one by a month and the other's death by more, it would be contrary to the time added to the divorce. And his statement: 'and it' i.e. the condition of concurrency of their deaths or arrivals is impossible by custom.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This final passage of the window refers to an objection raised by al-Razi (likely Fakhr al-Din al-Razi) against the Hanafi ruling. Al-Razi argued that by strict analogy (qiyas), the divorce should not occur unless both persons die or arrive at the same time (muqtarinan). He claimed that if one dies a month later than the other, the time of divorce would not match the stated condition. The text responds that requiring such conjunction (qiran) is practically impossible (muhal 'aadan – impossible customarily). Therefore, the Hanafi position based on istihsan (juridical preference) is valid, allowing the divorce to take effect retroactively based on the first death or arrival. This refutes al-Razi's objection by showing that the analogy fails due to practical impossibility.

Key Terms
قرآن (qur'ān): In this context, it refers to the conjunction (qiran) of two events, not the Quran.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juridical preference that overrides strict analogy due to necessity or custom.

Suspended Divorce Before Death of Two Persons: Istinad vs Iqtisar
Ruling on divorce suspended on death of two persons within a month

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between istinad and iqtisar in suspended divorce cases and identify the basis for the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding the determination of the month.

Core Idea
When simultaneous occurrence of conditions is impossible, istihsan reinterprets the condition as consecutive, not concurrent.

This passage explores a delicate issue in suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq) where the condition refers to two events: the death of two persons within a specified timeframe. The central question is whether the divorce takes effect upon the occurrence of the first event or must wait for both. The Hanafi school is divided: Imam Abu Hanifa uses istinad (retroactive reference) while the Sahibayn employ iqtisar (restriction). Understanding this distinction requires careful analysis of the interplay between custom (urf) and legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional phrase and its elements
The husband says 'You are divorced one month before the death of Zaid and Amr'. The condition involves two deaths and a time period. Determine what must occur for the condition to be fulfilled.
The phrase 'one month before' attaches the divorce to a specific month relative to both deaths.
2
Determine the scenario when one dies within the month vs after
If one dies before a month has passed from the utterance, the condition fails because the 'beforeness' is lost. If one dies after a month, the divorce becomes effective, but the school differs on the mechanism.
Death after a month triggers the ruling; the timing of the second death affects only the legal characterization.
3
Distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Abu Hanifa: divorce occurs by istinad (reference back) to the beginning of the month when the first dies. Sahibayn: divorce occurs by iqtisar (restriction) at the beginning of the month, without waiting for the second death.
Both agree the month is determined by the first death, but the Sahibayn do not see retroactive effect.
4
Understand the basis of istihsan over qiyas
Analogy (qiyas) would require simultaneous occurrence (qiran) of both deaths, but this is customarily impossible. Istihsan overrides qiyas: the speaker's customary intent is consecutive timing, not simultaneous.
Al-Razi's objection based on qiyas is rejected because it leads to impossibility.
5
Contrast with the case of arrival (qudum)
If the condition is 'before the arrival of Zaid and Amr', the month is not determined because the second arrival may never happen. The divorce waits until both arrive. In death, the second death is inevitable, so the month is fixed.
Certainty of the second event is key: death is certain, arrival is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال أي لو قال لامرأته أنت طالق قبل موت زيد وعمرو بشهر فمات أحدهما قبل شهر من وقت الكلام فات الوصف وهو القبلية على موتهما بشهر ففات الموصوف وهو الوقت المضاف إليه الطلاق فتعذر الوقوع، وإن مات أحدهما بعد شهر وقع مستنداً عنده إلى أول الشهر مقتصراً عندهما لا ينتظر موت الآخر لتعين الشهر المضاف إليه الطلاق وهو المتصل بأول الكائنين وهما موت زيد وعمرو لا محالة لأنه لم يبق للثاني تأثير في إيجاد الشرط فلا يتوقف عليه فصار كأنت طالق قبل الفطر والأضحى بشهر يقع في أول رمضان ولا ينتظر ما بعده، وهذا بخلاف القدوم في أنت طالق قبل قدوم زيد وعمرو بشهر لا يقع ما لم يقدم الآخر لعدم تعين الشهر المضاف إليه الطلاق عند اتصاله بأولهما لجواز أن لا يقدم الآخر أصلاً فكان للثاني تأثير في إيجاد الشرط، فإذا قدم طلقت بطريق الاقتصار خلافاً لزفر، أما في الموت فيتعين الشهر بموت أحدهما لكون موت الآخر كائناً لا محالة قوله : (والقرآن) مبتدأ خبره قوله مبنى طعن الرازي وهو إشارة إلى أن القياس في الصورتين أنه لا يقع الطلاق ما لم يقترن موتهما أو قدومهما وهو الذي بنى عليه الرازي طعنه في هذه المسألة لأنه لو وقع بعد موت أحدهما بشهر وموت الآخر بأكثر كان خلاف الوقت المضاف إليه الطلاق وقوله (وهو) أي اشتراط قران موتهما أو قدومهما محال عادة وجه الاستحسان لأن الإنسان لا يريد بكلامه الممتنع عادة بل المعتاد وذلك شهر قبل موتهما على التعاقب لا القرآن كما في قبل الفطر والأضحى بشهر قوله : كذا قبل أن تحيضي حيضة بشهر ورأت الدم ثلاثاً، وقبل قدوم زيد وموت عمرو وقدم لأن الباقي كائن بخلاف ما لو مات عمرو ا.هـ. وتوضيحه في شرح الفارسي.
And if he said – meaning if he said to his wife: 'You are divorced one month before the death of Zaid and Amr', and one of them died before a month from the time of the speech, then the description is lost, which is the 'beforeness' regarding their death by a month, so the described [time] is lost, which is the time to which the divorce is attached, so occurrence becomes impossible. And if one of them died after a month, it occurs by reference (istinad) according to him (Abu Hanifa) to the beginning of the month, by restriction (iqtisar) according to both (Sahibayn); he does not wait for the death of the other because the month to which the divorce is attached is determined, and it is connected to the first of the two events, which are the death of Zaid and Amr inevitably, because there remains for the second no effect in bringing about the condition, so he does not wait for it. Thus it becomes like 'you are divorced one month before Fitr and Adha' – it occurs at the beginning of Ramadan and does not wait for what comes after. This is unlike arrival (qudum) in 'you are divorced one month before the arrival of Zaid and Amr' – it does not occur until the other arrives, because the month to which the divorce is attached is not determined when it is connected to the first of them, since it is possible that the other never arrives at all, so the second has effect in bringing about the condition. Thus when he arrives, she is divorced by way of restriction (iqtisar), contrary to Zufar. As for death, the month is determined by the death of one because the death of the other is inevitable. His saying: 'and the conjunction (qiran)' – its subject is 'the building of al-Razi's objection' – it indicates that the analogy (qiyas) in both cases is that divorce does not occur unless their death or arrival coincides (qiran), and that is what al-Razi built his objection on in this issue, because if it occurred after the death of one by a month and the death of the other by more, it would be contrary to the time to which divorce is attached. His saying: 'and it' – meaning the condition of conjunction of their death or arrival is impossible by custom. The basis of istihsan is that a person does not intend by his speech what is impossible by custom, but rather the customary [meaning], which is a month before their deaths consecutively, not simultaneously, just as in 'one month before Fitr and Adha'. His saying: 'likewise before you menstruate one month' and she saw blood for three days, and before the arrival of Zaid and the death of Amr, and he arrived because the remaining [event] is certain, unlike if Amr died [first]... end of quote. Its explanation is in Sharh al-Farisi.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage addresses a complex case of suspended divorce (ta'liq al-talaq). A man says to his wife: 'You are divorced one month before the death of Zaid and Amr.' The ruling depends on timing. If one dies before a month has passed from the utterance, the condition fails because the required 'beforeness' (qabliyya) is lost. If one dies after a month, the divorce occurs by istinad (reference back) to the beginning of that month according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but by iqtisar (restriction) according to the Sahibayn. The difference is that Abu Hanifa sees the month as determined by the first death, while the Sahibayn require the second death to occur before the divorce is effective, but since death is inevitable, the divorce is restricted to the beginning of the month after the first death. The text distinguishes this from a case of arrival (qudum), where the second person might never arrive, so the divorce is suspended until both arrive. The disputation of al-Razi is mentioned: he argued that analogy (qiyas) requires simultaneous occurrence (qiran) of both events, but this is customarily impossible, so istihsan (juristic preference) applies by interpreting the phrase as 'consecutively' (ta'aqub) rather than simultaneously, similar to saying 'one month before Eid al-Fitr and Eid al-Adha', which means before the first of the two Eids. The text also provides analogies to menstruation and to cases where one event is certain (death) and the other is not (arrival). This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf with the Sahibayn.

Key Terms
استناد (istinad): Legal reference of an event back to an earlier time
اقتصار (iqtisar): Restriction of the effect to the moment the condition is met
قران (qiran): Simultaneous occurrence of two events as a condition

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'You are divorced one month before the death of Zaid and Amr', and Zaid dies after two months while Amr dies after three months, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) No divorce occurs because the timing is violated
B) Divorce occurs at the beginning of the month before Zaid's death by istinad (Abu Hanifa) or by iqtisar (Sahibayn)
C) Divorce occurs only when both have died
D) The marriage continues because death is not a valid condition

Key Takeaway
In suspended divorce with two conditions, when simultaneous occurrence is impossible, istihsan allows the divorce to take effect upon the first fulfilled condition.

Divorce Suspended on Longer Life: The Concept of Istinad
Ruling on suspended divorce with condition of longer life and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the 'longer-lived' divorce and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding istinad vs iqtisar.

Core Idea
In a suspended divorce conditioned on death, the divorce occurs retroactively (istinad) according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn require it to be when the condition is met (iqtisar).

This lesson examines a specific suspensive condition: a man says to his two wives, 'The longer-lived of you is divorced now.' The ruling depends on whether the divorce takes effect immediately upon utterance or only when the condition is fulfilled. The Hanafi school has a well-known internal disagreement on this point, which we will analyze using the text from Fath al-Qadir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its effect
The husband says, 'The longer-lived of you is divorced now.' Identify the condition (death of one wife) and determine when the divorce takes effect according to the text.
The text states 'لم يقع حتى تموت إحداهما' – it does not occur until one dies.
2
Understand the mechanism of istinad
The text says 'فإذا ماتت طلقت الأخرى مستنداً' – when she dies, the other is divorced mustanidan (by reference). This means the divorce refers back to the time of utterance. Contrast with iqtisar (occurring at the moment of condition).
Istinad is a unique Hanafi concept.
3
Identify the conflicting views
Recognize that Abu Hanifa holds istinad, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold iqtisar. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The source text only presents Abu Hanifa's view; the dispute is known from other works.
4
Determine the practical consequence
Consider the thamarah: if the 'surviving' wife remarries or inherits between the utterance and the death, the ruling affects validity. Under istinad, actions during that period are affected; under iqtisar, they are not.
This highlights the importance of the dispute.
5
Note the authority level
The text is from Fath al-Qadir, a later Hanafi work. The dispute is recorded in other sources as well. No explicit tarjih is given here.
This is a mutakhkhirin source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتح القدير : ولو قال أطولكما حياة طالق الساعة لم يقع حتى تموت إحداهما فإذا ماتت طلقت الأخرى مستنداً ا هـ . . وفي المحيط : أنت طالق إلى قريب فهو إلى ما نوى لأن مدة الدنيا كلها قريبة، وإن لم ينو فإلى أن يمضي شهر إلا يوماً. وفي الذخيرة : أنت طالق الساعة واحدة وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعت واحدة للحال بنصف الألف والأخرى غداً بغير شيء، وإن تزوجها قبل مجيء الغد ثم جاء وقعت أخرى بخمسمائة . ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعت واحدة للحال بغير شيء، فإذا جاء الغد وقعت أخرى بألف. ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم تطليقة بائنة وغداً أخرى بألف يقع للحال تطليقة بائنة بغير شيء، فإذا جاء الغد وقعت أخرى بغير شيء. ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقع اليوم واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بالألف ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى أملك الرجعة بألف درهم انصرف البدل إليهما فتقع اليوم واحدة بخمسمائة وغداً أخرى بغير شيء إلا أن يتزوجها كما إذا لم يضف أصلاً، وكذا إذا قال أنت طالق الساعة ثلاثاً وغداً أخرى بائنة أو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بغير شيء بألف درهم، فالبدل ينصرف إليهما فيقع اليوم واحدة بخمسمائة
And in Fath al-Qadir: 'If he said to his two wives: The longer-lived of you is divorced now, it does not occur until one of them dies, and when she dies, the other is divorced by reference (mustanidan).' End quote. And in al-Muhit: 'You are divorced close (ila qarib), then it is according to his intention, because the entire duration of the world is close; and if he did not intend, then until a month less a day passes.' And in al-Dhakhira: 'You are divorced one now and another tomorrow for one thousand, and she accepted: one occurs now for half the thousand, and the other occurs tomorrow for nothing. And if he marries her before the coming of tomorrow, then when tomorrow comes, another occurs for five hundred.' And if he said, 'You are divorced one now with the right of return, and another tomorrow for one thousand,' and she accepted: one occurs now for nothing, so when tomorrow comes, another occurs for one thousand. And if he said, 'You are divorced today a irrevocable divorce (ba'in), and another tomorrow for one thousand,' an irrevocable divorce occurs now for nothing, and when tomorrow comes, another occurs for nothing. And if he said, 'You are divorced today one for nothing, and another tomorrow for one thousand,' and she accepted: one occurs today for nothing and tomorrow another for the thousand. And if he said, 'You are divorced one now with the right of return, and another tomorrow with the right of return for one thousand dirhams,' the consideration (badal) is distributed to both, so one occurs today for five hundred and tomorrow another for nothing unless he marries her, just as if he did not add anything. And likewise if he said, 'You are divorced three now and another tomorrow irrevocably,' or he said, 'You are divorced one now for nothing and another tomorrow for nothing for one thousand dirhams,' the consideration is distributed to both, so one occurs today for five hundred...
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This section collects rulings from multiple Hanafi works (Fath al-Qadir, al-Muhit, al-Dhakhira) on various suspended divorce scenarios. First, from Fath al-Qadir: if a man says to his two wives 'The longer-lived of you is divorced now,' the divorce does not occur until one dies; then the surviving wife is divorced retroactively (mustanidan) to the time of utterance. This is another example of istinad. The text notes an intra-Hanafi difference: 'عنده ومقتصراً عندهما' as in the previous lesson. Second, from al-Muhit: if he says 'You are divorce close (ila qarib),' it depends on his intention; if no intention, it means a month less a day (i.e., a short period). Third, from al-Dhakhira, a series of cases where a husband combines immediate and future divorces with a payment (badal). The key principle is how the consideration is allocated when multiple divorces are promised. For example, if he says 'one now and another tomorrow for a thousand,' and she accepts, the first divorce occurs now for half the thousand (since the second is also part of the contract), and the second occurs tomorrow for nothing (even if he remarries her before that, then it occurs for five hundred). If the first divorce is with right of return (raj'i), the first occurs without payment, and the second occurs with the full thousand. If the first is irrevocable (ba'in), it occurs for nothing, and the second also for nothing. The general rule is that if the badal is mentioned for both, it is divided equally between them. If the second is conditional on remarriage, the payment adjusts accordingly.

Key Terms
مستنداً (mustanidan): Referring back to the original time of the statement; retroactive effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir, when does the divorce take effect in the 'longer-lived' case?
A) Immediately upon utterance
B) At the moment one wife dies, retroactively to utterance
C) At the moment one wife dies, forward from that moment
D) It does not occur at all

Key Takeaway
When a divorce is suspended on a condition, the timing of its effect can be retroactive (istinad) or immediate upon condition (iqtisar), depending on the school's interpretation.

Interpreting Ambiguous Time Phrases in Divorce: The Case of 'Close'
Ruling on interpreting ambiguous time phrase in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that ambiguous time expressions in talaq are interpreted according to the husband's intention, and state the default ruling when intention is unknown.

Core Idea
Words like 'close' in divorce are interpreted by the husband's real intention; if unknown, they mean a month less a day.

Sometimes a husband uses vague terms like 'close' to specify when a divorce takes effect. Hanafi fiqh provides a clear method: first try to ascertain the husband's intention, and if that is impossible, a default period is assigned. This lesson from al-Muhit illustrates the principle using the word 'qarib' (close).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous term
The husband says 'You are divorced close (ila qarib).' Recognize this as an ambiguous time expression.
The Arabic 'ila qarib' can mean 'soon' or 'in a short time'.
2
Apply the primary rule: intention
The text says 'فهو إلى ما نوى' – it is according to his intention. The husband's real meaning is taken.
This is based on the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات'.
3
Apply the default rule if intention unknown
If intention is not known, the default is 'a month less a day'. The text gives the reason: 'because the entire duration of the world is close' – so a specific limit is set.
The default avoids uncertainty (gharar).
4
Understand the reasoning
The text explains that the whole world is 'close' in one sense, so without a limit the term would be meaningless. A month less a day is a known short period in Hanafi fiqh.
Compare with other defaults in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This section collects rulings from multiple Hanafi works (Fath al-Qadir, al-Muhit, al-Dhakhira) on various suspended divorce scenarios. First, from Fath al-Qadir: if a man says to his two wives 'The longer-lived of you is divorced now,' the divorce does not occur until one dies; then the surviving wife is divorced retroactively (mustanidan) to the time of utterance. If the second is conditional on remarriage, the payment adjusts accordingly.

Allocation of Badal in Combined Immediate and Future Divorces
Rulings on allocation of badal in combined immediate and future divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the allocation of badal (consideration) in combined divorce promises based on the wording and type of divorce (raj'i, ba'in).

Core Idea
When a husband promises multiple divorces with a payment, the badal is divided equally between them unless the first divorce is revocable or irrevocable, which affects the amount due.

This lesson presents a series of cases from al-Dhakhira where a husband combines an immediate divorce with a future divorce and offers a sum of money (badal). The allocation of the consideration depends on the type of divorce (revocable raj'i or irrevocable ba'in) and whether remarriage occurs. These detailed scenarios illustrate the Hanafi approach to contractual conditions in khul'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic scenario
Start with the simplest case: 'You are divorced one now and another tomorrow for one thousand.' Identify the two divorces and the total badal.
The first divorce is immediate, second is future.
2
Determine allocation of badal
In the first case, the badal is divided equally: 500 for the first divorce, and the second divorce occurs for nothing (since the contract is considered one transaction).
Exception: if he remarries her before the second divorce, then the second occurs with 500.
3
Analyze variations with different divorce types
Examine cases where the first divorce is raj'i (revocable) or ba'in (irrevocable). In raj'i, the first divorce occurs for nothing because the husband retains the right to return; in ba'in, both occur for nothing.
The type affects the allocation.
4
Apply the general rule
The text states that if the badal is mentioned for both divorces, it is distributed to both. If the first is raj'i, it gets half; if ba'in, it gets nothing.
This is the key principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي فتح القدير : ولو قال أطولكما حياة طالق الساعة لم يقع حتى تموت إحداهما فإذا ماتت طلقت الأخرى مستنداً ا هـ . . وفي المحيط : أنت طالق إلى قريب فهو إلى ما نوى لأن مدة الدنيا كلها قريبة، وإن لم ينو فإلى أن يمضي شهر إلا يوماً. وفي الذخيرة : أنت طالق الساعة واحدة وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعت واحدة للحال بنصف الألف والأخرى غداً بغير شيء، وإن تزوجها قبل مجيء الغد ثم جاء وقعت أخرى بخمسمائة . ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقعت واحدة للحال بغير شيء، فإذا جاء الغد وقعت أخرى بألف. ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم تطليقة بائنة وغداً أخرى بألف يقع للحال تطليقة بائنة بغير شيء، فإذا جاء الغد وقعت أخرى بغير شيء. ولو قال أنت طالق اليوم واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بألف فقبلت وقع اليوم واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بالألف ولو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة أملك الرجعة وغداً أخرى أملك الرجعة بألف درهم انصرف البدل إليهما فتقع اليوم واحدة بخمسمائة وغداً أخرى بغير شيء إلا أن يتزوجها كما إذا لم يضف أصلاً، وكذا إذا قال أنت طالق الساعة ثلاثاً وغداً أخرى بائنة أو قال أنت طالق الساعة واحدة بغير شيء وغداً أخرى بغير شيء بألف درهم، فالبدل ينصرف إليهما فيقع اليوم واحدة بخمسمائة
And in Fath al-Qadir: 'If he said to his two wives: The longer-lived of you is divorced now, it does not occur until one of them dies, and when she dies, the other is divorced by reference (mustanidan).' End quote. And in al-Muhit: 'You are divorced close (ila qarib), then it is according to his intention, because the entire duration of the world is close; and if he did not intend, then until a month less a day passes.' And in al-Dhakhira: 'You are divorced one now and another tomorrow for one thousand, and she accepted: one occurs now for half the thousand, and the other occurs tomorrow for nothing. And if he marries her before the coming of tomorrow, then when tomorrow comes, another occurs for five hundred.' And if he said, 'You are divorced one now with the right of return, and another tomorrow for one thousand,' and she accepted: one occurs now for nothing, so when tomorrow comes, another occurs for one thousand. And if he said, 'You are divorced today a irrevocable divorce (ba'in), and another tomorrow for one thousand,' an irrevocable divorce occurs now for nothing, and when tomorrow comes, another occurs for nothing. And if he said, 'You are divorced today one for nothing, and another tomorrow for one thousand,' and she accepted: one occurs today for nothing and tomorrow another for the thousand. And if he said, 'You are divorced one now with the right of return, and another tomorrow with the right of return for one thousand dirhams,' the consideration (badal) is distributed to both, so one occurs today for five hundred and tomorrow another for nothing unless he marries her, just as if he did not add anything. And likewise if he said, 'You are divorced three now and another tomorrow irrevocably,' or he said, 'You are divorced one now for nothing and another tomorrow for nothing for one thousand dirhams,' the consideration is distributed to both, so one occurs today for five hundred...
Source pages p. 487

Commentary
This section collects rulings from multiple Hanafi works (Fath al-Qadir, al-Muhit, al-Dhakhira) on various suspended divorce scenarios. First, from Fath al-Qadir: if a man says to his two wives 'The longer-lived of you is divorced now,' the divorce does not occur until one dies; then the surviving wife is divorced retroactively (mustanidan) to the time of utterance. This is another example of istinad. The text notes an intra-Hanafi difference: 'عنده ومقتصراً عندهما' as in the previous lesson. Second, from al-Muhit: if he says 'You are divorce close (ila qarib),' it depends on his intention; if no intention, it means a month less a day (i.e., a short period). Third, from al-Dhakhira, a series of cases where a husband combines immediate and future divorces with a payment (badal). The key principle is how the consideration is allocated when multiple divorces are promised. For example, if he says 'one now and another tomorrow for a thousand,' and she accepts, the first divorce occurs now for half the thousand (since the second is also part of the contract), and the second occurs tomorrow for nothing (even if he remarries her before that, then it occurs for five hundred). If the first divorce is with right of return (raj'i), the first occurs without payment, and the second occurs with the full thousand. If the first is irrevocable (ba'in), it occurs for nothing, and the second also for nothing. The general rule is that if the badal is mentioned for both, it is divided equally between them. If the second is conditional on remarriage, the payment adjusts accordingly.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Consideration paid by the wife in exchange for divorce
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says, 'You are divorced one now with the right of return and another tomorrow for 1000,' how much is due for the first divorce?
A) 500
B) 1000
C) Nothing
D) 250

Key Takeaway
The allocation of badal in combined divorces depends on the type of each divorce: equally split for similar types, free for the first if raj'i, and free for both if the first is ba'in.

Ten Scenarios of Describing the Second Talaq
Parsing the ten possibilities when describing the second talaq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to enumerate the ten scenarios of describing the second talaq in a suspended divorce and apply the rule that the description of the second talaq is void.

Core Idea
Describing the second talaq is void; it always occurs unconditionally.

In Hanafi law, when a husband pronounces a suspended talaq (e.g., 'today one, tomorrow another'), any description he attaches only to the second talaq is ineffective. This lesson breaks down the ten logical possibilities that arise from describing the first talaq, the second, both, or neither with one of three attributes: raj'ah (right to take back), baynunah (irrevocability), or bi-ghayr shay' (without financial consideration). Understanding this taxonomy helps you apply the rule correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Understand the base scenario
The husband says 'You are divorced today one, and tomorrow another' without any description. This is the baseline: each talaq occurs with half the specified amount (if any) and without condition.
The amount is split equally unless specified otherwise.
2
Learn that describing the second talaq is void
If the husband describes only the second talaq (e.g., with raj'ah, baynunah, or bi-ghayr shay' for a price), the description is void because it is attached to a future event. The second talaq occurs unconditionally when the time comes.
The first talaq is still affected proportionally: it takes half the price if the price was for both.
3
Identify the three possible descriptions
Each talaq can be described with: (1) raj'ah – revocable, (2) baynunah – irrevocable, or (3) bi-ghayr shay' – without anything. Or it can be left undescribed.
These are the only descriptions relevant in this parsing.
4
Enumerate the ten combinations
For each talaq (first and second), there are 5 possibilities: undescribed, described with raj'ah, baynunah, or bi-ghayr shay'. But the second talaq's description is void, so effectively only the first talaq's description matters. The ten scenarios arise from: (a) neither described, (b) first described with one of the three, (c) second described but void, so same as (a) for second, plus (d) both described (second void). So total = 1 (none) + 3 (first only) + 3 (second only, but second void) + 3 (both, second void) = 10? Actually the text says 10. Let's list: 1. Neither described; 2-4. First only: raj'ah, baynunah, bi-ghayr shay'; 5-7. Second only: raj'ah, baynunah, bi-ghayr shay' (but second void); 8-10. Both: first raj'ah + second void, etc. That gives 10.
For the second only cases, the ruling is identical to neither described because the description is void.
5
Apply the rule to a specific example
Example: 'You are divorced today one, and tomorrow another, with the right to take back for a thousand.' The second description is void, so the first talaq occurs with 500 (half of the price for both talaqs) and the second occurs unconditionally without any price.
If the second description were baynunah, the first talaq still takes 500, and the second occurs as a regular talaq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغداً أخرى بغير شيء. ولو وصف الثانية فقط بأن قال أنت طالق اليوم واحدة وغداً أخرى أملك الرجعة بألف أو بغير شيء بألف أو بائنة بألف لغا ذلك الوصف فتقع واحدة اليوم بخمسمائة وأخرى بغير شيء إلا أن يتزوجها، فصار الحاصل أن الوجوه عشرة لأنه إما أن لا يصف واحدة منهما أو يصف الأولى فقط إما بالرجعة أو بالبينونة أو بكونها بغير شيء أو يصف الثانية فقط كذلك أو يصفهما جميعاً كذلك فليتأمل.
And tomorrow another (talaq) without anything. And if he described the second only by saying, 'You are divorced today one, and tomorrow another, I retain the right to take you back for a thousand, or without anything for a thousand, or irrevocably for a thousand,' that description is void, so one (talaq) occurs today for five hundred, and another without anything, unless he marries her. So the conclusion is that the aspects are ten, because either he does not describe either of them, or he describes the first only, either with return (رجعة) or with finality (بينونة) or with being without anything; or he describes the second only likewise; or he describes both likewise. So let it be pondered.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of describing only the second talaq in a suspended statement. The author explains that if a man says, 'You are divorced today one, and tomorrow another, and I retain the right to take you back for a thousand, or without anything for a thousand, or irrevocably for a thousand,' the description of the second talaq is void because it is attached to a future time. The first talaq takes effect immediately with half the specified amount (since the full amount was for both), and the second talaq occurs without any condition when the future time arrives, unless he remarries her in the case of an irrevocable divorce. The passage then enumerates ten possible scenarios based on whether the first, second, both, or neither talaq is described, and whether the description is with 'رجعة' (right to take back), 'بينونة' (irrevocability), or 'بغير شيء' (without anything). This is a classic Hanafi parsing exercise to cover all possibilities.

Key Terms
الرجعة (al-raj'ah): In this context, a description of the talaq meaning that the husband retains the right to take back his wife during her 'iddah period.
البينونة (al-baynunah): A description meaning an irrevocable divorce that severs the marital bond completely.
بغير شيء (bi-ghayr shay'): A description meaning that the talaq occurs without any financial consideration.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Both talaqs occur with the condition of a thousand each.
B) The first talaq occurs with five hundred, and the second with a thousand.
C) The first talaq occurs with five hundred, and the second without anything.

Key Takeaway
In a suspended talaq, any description attached only to the second talaq is void, so the second talaq always occurs unconditionally.

Ruling on 'Qabil' in Talaq: Correction by Abu al-Fadl
Clarifying the meaning of 'qabil' and correcting a previous fatwa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the correct Hanafi ruling for the word 'qabil' in divorce formulations, distinguishing between time-based and event-based conditions.

Core Idea
The word 'qabil' in a divorce formula does not always mean 'just before'; its meaning depends on the attached condition.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq quotes a fatwa from Tatimmat al-Fatawa and then provides a critical correction by Abu al-Fadl. The issue is the interpretation of the word 'qabil' (before) when used in a suspended divorce. Understanding this nuance is essential for muftis to issue accurate rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original fatwa's ruling
The original fatwa states that if a man says 'You are divorced before (qabil) tomorrow and before the arrival of so-and-so', the divorce occurs a blink of an eye before the event, because 'qabil' indicates a short time. Note the basis: qabil is considered a time adverb.
2
Analyze Abu al-Fadl's correction
Abu al-Fadl declares the original answer for 'qabil arrival' as incorrect. He states the correct view: the divorce occurs at the moment of arrival, not before. This shows that 'qabil' when attached to an event does not imply immediacy but conditionality.
The correction highlights the need to consider the nature of the conditioned event.
3
Examine the analogous case (Dhu al-Uqdah)
Abu al-Fadl provides an analogy: if someone says 'If it is Dhu al-Uqdah (a specific month), you are divorced', and some of that time has passed, then she is divorced at the moment of speaking. This reinforces that the timing depends on the condition's nature.
This analogy helps understand that when the condition is a time period, the divorce takes effect immediately if part of that time has elapsed.
4
Derive the ruling for 'qabil' with an event
The key distinction: when 'qabil' is followed by a future time (like tomorrow), it indicates a brief moment before. But when followed by an event (like arrival), it indicates the event itself as the trigger. Thus, the word 'qabil' is ambiguous and must be interpreted contextually.
This is a critical refinement of the earlier fatwa.
5
Apply the corrected ruling
In practice, a mufti should examine the exact wording. If the husband says 'You are divorced before the arrival of so-and-so', the divorce occurs upon arrival, not before. If he says 'before tomorrow', it occurs a blink before tomorrow.
The ruling ensures that the intention is honored and ambiguity is resolved.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي تتمة الفتاوى : أنت طالق قبيل غد وقبيل قدوم فلان فهو قبل ذلك بطرفة عين لأن قبيل وقت. قال أبو الفضل : هذا هو الجواب في قوله قبيل قدوم فلان غير صحيح، والصحيح أنه يقع الطلاق إذا قدم فلان، فلو قال إذا كان ذو العقدة فأنت طالق وقد مضى بعضه فهي طالق ساعة ما تكلم ا هـ. وقد ذكرنا هذه المسائل تتميماً للطلاق المضاف تكثيراً للفوائد والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وهو الميسر لكل عسير .
And in Tatimmat al-Fatawa: 'You are divorced before (qabil) tomorrow and before the arrival of so-and-so — it is before that by a blink of an eye, because qabil is a time.' Abu al-Fadl said: 'This is the answer. Regarding his statement "before the arrival of so-and-so", it is not correct. The correct view is that the divorce occurs when so-and-so arrives. So if he said, "If it is Dhu al-'Uqdah (a specific time), you are divorced," and some of it has passed, then she is divorced at the moment he spoke.' He said: 'We have mentioned these issues as a completion for the suspended divorce, multiplying benefits, and Allah is most knowing and He is the Facilitator of every difficulty.'
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage quotes a ruling from Tatimmat al-Fatawa regarding the word 'قبيل' (qabil, meaning 'before'). The original fatwa states that if a man says, 'You are divorced before tomorrow and before the arrival of so-and-so,' the divorce occurs at the earliest time before that event, by a blink of an eye, because 'قبيل' indicates a time. However, Abu al-Fadl corrects this, saying that the correct view is that the divorce occurs upon the actual arrival of so-and-so, not before. He provides an analogy: if someone says, 'If it is Dhu al-'Uqdah (a time in the month), you are divorced,' and some of that time has already passed, then she is divorced at the moment he speaks. This refinement is important because it shows that the meaning of 'before' can be ambiguous and needs clarification based on context.

Key Terms
قبيل (qabil): The word meaning 'before' in the context of time; it indicates a brief time preceding the mentioned event.
ذو العقدة (Dhu al-Uqdah): A specific time period mentioned in the text, possibly a month or season.
تتمة الفتاوى (Tatimmat al-Fatawa): A collection of fatwas; the source of the original ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At the moment he says it.
B) A blink of an eye before the arrival.
C) At the moment of the arrival.
D) It is invalid because it is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
The word 'qabil' in a suspended divorce must be interpreted contextually: with time-based conditions it indicates a brief moment before, but with event-based conditions it triggers the divorce upon the event itself.

When 'I am divorced from you' is Void: Distinguishing Valid and Invalid Divorce Phrases
Explaining the ruling on 'أنا منك طالق' and differentiating it from other phrases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the phrases 'أنا منك طالق', 'أنا منك بائن', and 'عليك حرام', and explain why some are void while others are effective based on the locus of talaq.

Core Idea
Talaq targets the wife's ownership, not the husband's; 'I am divorced from you' is void, but 'I am bain from you' can be valid with intention.

The matn states that 'أنا منك طالق' (I am divorced from you) is void even with intention. The commentator expands this to clarify that phrases like 'أنا منك بائن' and 'عليك حرام' are effective when intended, because they remove the connection of marriage, which is shared between spouses. Understanding the precise wording and its attachment is crucial for divorce to take effect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Phrase and Its Attachment
Determine whether the phrase attaches the divorce to the husband (e.g., 'أنا منك طالق') or to the wife (e.g., 'أنت طالق'). Also check if the word is 'طالق', 'بائن', or 'حرام'.
2
Apply the Principle of Locus (Mahall)
Talaq removes the marital ownership (milk) which resides with the wife. Therefore, divorce must be directed at the wife. Phrases directed at the husband are void because they attach divorce to a non-locus.
The locus of talaq is the wife, not the husband.
3
Distinguish Between Talaq, Ibanah, and Tahrim
While 'talaq' removes ownership, 'ibānah' removes the marital connection (silā), and 'taḥrīm' removes permissibility (ḥill). These concepts are shared between spouses, so phrases like 'أنا منك بائن' are valid because they address the shared connection.
Ibanah and tahrim remove something common to both, so they can be attached to either spouse.
4
Check for Intention and Additional Words
For phrases like 'أنا منك بائن', intention is required for the divorce to occur. If the husband says 'أنا بائن' without 'منك', it is void even with intention. The opposite applies if directed to the wife: 'أنت بائن' is valid with intention.
The phrase 'عليك حرام' is similar to 'you are haram upon me' — it requires intention but is effective.
5
Evaluate the Error in Khazanat al-Akmal
The commentator corrects a mistake where it was claimed that 'أنت حرام' or 'بائن' said by the husband is void. The correct view is that such phrases are valid when addressed to the wife, but were discussed in the context of the wife speaking to the husband.
This step highlights the importance of careful transmission and verification of legal rulings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أنا منك طالق لغو وإن نوى وتبين في البائن والحرام يعني إذا قال أنا منك بائن أو عليك حرام فإنها تبين بالنية والفرق أن الطلاق لإزالة الملك الثابت بالنكاح أو القيد فمحل الطلاق محلهما وهي محلهما ،دونه فالإضافة إليه إضافة الطلاق إلى غير محله فيلغو. وأما حجره عن أختها أو خامسة فليس موجب نكاحها بل حجر شرعي ثابت ابتداء عن الجمع بين الأختين وخمس لا حكماً للنكاح ، ولهذا لو تزوجها مع أختها معاً أو منه حيث نقله من العيون، وفي العيون ذكر ذلك من جانب المرأة فقال : لو جعل أمر امرأته بيدها فقالت للزوج أنت علي حرام أو فليتأمل قوله : (وفي خزانة الأكمل (ع) قال الرملي : أي معزياً إلى العيون كما صرح به في النهر ا هـ . واعلم أن خزانه الأكمل اسم كتاب في ست مجلدات تصنيف أبي عبد الله يوسف بن علي بن محمد الجرجاني ونسب لأبي الليث والصحيح أنه .لهذا كذا في تاج التراجم للعلامة قاسم . والحرام أنت طالق واحدة إليه وإن أضاف إلى نفسه لا يقع من غير إضافة إليها، وإن خيرها فأجابت بالحرمة أو البينونة فلا بد من الجمع بين الإضافتين أنت حرام علي، أنا حرام عليك أنت بائن مني أنا بائن منك والله سبحانه وتعالى الموفق . وقد حكى في المعراج في مسألة أنا منك طالق أن امرأة قالت لزوجها لو كان إلي ما إليك لرأيت الله ماذا أصنع فقال جعلت ما إلي إليك فقالت طلقتك فرفع ذلك إلى ابن عباس رضي عنهما فقال : خطأ الله نوءها هلا قالت طلقت نفسي منك، وروي خط الله وصوبه النسفي ، وقال : لا يجوز خطأ، وصاحب الفائق عكسه. والنوء كوكب تستمطر به العرب ا هـ .
His statement: 'I am divorced from you is void, even if he intends, and it is clarified in the bain and haram.' That is, if he says, 'I am bain from you' or 'haram upon you', then she becomes bain with intention. The difference is that talaq is for removing the ownership established by marriage or the restriction, so the locus of talaq is the ownership and the restriction, and she is the locus of them, not him, so attaching talaq to him is attaching it to a non-locus, so it is void. As for his preventing her from her sister or a fifth wife, that is not a cause of her marriage, but a legal restriction established ab initio from combining sisters or five wives, not a ruling of marriage. Hence, if he marries her together with her sister or joins them together, it is not permissible, unlike ibanah because its wording is for removing the connection, and the connection of marriage is shared between them, so its attachment to each is valid if one knows its reality. And unlike tahrim because it is for removing permissibility, which is shared. We restricted it with our saying 'from you' and 'upon you' because if he says 'I am bain' or 'I made myself bain' without saying 'from you', or 'haram' without saying 'upon you', she is not divorced even if he intends, because baynunah is transitive, as in al-Mi'raj, unlike if he says 'you are bain' or 'haram' without adding anything, where she is divorced if he intends, because it specifies removing the connection between them, unlike the first. And he indicated that if he grants her the power of divorce and she divorces him, it does not occur, as we have mentioned. In al-Qunyah: 'You are haram' or 'You are upon me haram' — talaq occurs without intention, and there is no need for the word 'upon' (?) ... So he said: If he says to her 'I am bain' without 'from you' or 'I am haram' without 'upon you', this is nothing, unlike if he says 'you are bain' or 'you are haram'. Radi Allahu anhu said: In Khazanat al-Akmal: if he says to her 'you are haram' or 'bain' without saying 'from me', it is void. This is a slip on his part in transmission from al-Uyun. In al-Uyun, that is mentioned from the woman's side: if he places the matter in his wife's hand and she says to the husband 'you are upon me haram' or ... So let it be pondered. His statement: (In Khazanat al-Akmal (?) al-Ramli said: it is attributed to al-Uyun as clarified in al-Nahr. Know that Khazanat al-Akmal is the name of a book in six volumes by Abu Abdullah Yusuf ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Jurjani, attributed to Abu al-Layth, but the correct attribution is to him. This is from Taj al-Tarajim by Allama Qasim. And (the phrase) 'haram, you are divorced once or not, or upon my death, or upon your death' is void. And if she is in his possession or a share of her, saying 'you are from me bain or haram' or 'I am upon you haram or bain' occurs. And if she says 'you are bain' or 'haram' without saying 'from me', it is void. And in some copies of al-Uyun: if he says without the feminine 't' (i.e., 'bain' with masculine form), and the author of al-Akmal thought it was a new issue and thought that if the husband said that to his wife it is void. Radi Allahu ta'ala anhu said: At this point, our teacher Najm al-A'immah al-Bukhari made an additional slip by adding the word 'her' and saying: if he says to her 'you are haram' or 'bain', it is void, while the issue with the feminine 't' is mentioned in al-Waqi'at al-Kubra al-Madaniyyah and other works in the issues of al-Uyun, so the slip of both is known. The conclusion from the rulings is that if he attaches the prohibition or baynunah to her, it occurs without attachment to himself, and if he attaches to himself, it does not occur without attachment to her. And if he gives her the choice and she responds with prohibition or baynunah, then both attachments are necessary: 'you are haram upon me, I am haram upon you, you are bain from me, I am bain from you.' And Allah is the granter of success. It is narrated in al-Mi'raj on the issue of 'I am divorced from you' that a woman said to her husband: 'If what I have were as what you have, I would see what God would do.' He said: 'I have made what I have belong to you.' She said: 'I divorce you.' This was raised to Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him), who said: 'May Allah cause her star to go astray (i.e., mistake). Why didn't she say: I divorce myself from you?' It is also narrated: 'May Allah make a mistake' (خط الله) and al-Nasafi approved it, saying: 'It is not permissible to say May He cause to err', while the author of al-Faiq reversed it. An-naw' (star) is a star from which Arabs seek rain.
Source pages p. 488

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the matn statement 'أنا منك طالق لغو' (I am divorced from you is void). The author explains that the phrase 'أنا منك طالق' is void because the locus of talaq is the marriage bond, which is attached to the wife, not to the husband. However, if the husband says 'أنا منك بائن' (I am irrevocably separated from you) or 'عليك حرام' (you are forbidden upon me), the divorce takes effect with intention, because the words 'بائن' and 'حرام' are designed to remove the connection of marriage, which is shared between both parties. The passage then distinguishes between attaching the words to oneself (which is void) and attaching them to the wife (which is valid). It also discusses a mistake in Khazanat al-Akmal regarding the wording 'أنت حرام أو بائن' when said by the husband, clarifying that the correct source (al-Uyun) mentions it from the wife's side. The conclusion provides a practical summary: if the husband says 'أنت حرام' or 'أنت بائن' without 'مني', it is effective? Actually the passage says if he adds the prohibition to her, it occurs without adding to himself. But if he says 'أنا بائن' without 'منك', it is void. Finally, a story from Ibn Abbas illustrates a similar mistake by a woman who said 'I divorce you' instead of 'I divorce myself from you', showing the importance of correct phrasing.

Key Terms
بائن (bā'in): A term meaning irrevocable divorce; it severs the marriage completely.
حرام (ḥarām): Here used as a term for declaring the wife forbidden, which can effect a divorce if intended.
الإبانة (al-ibānah): The act of making the divorce irrevocable; the wording that removes the marital connection.
التحريم (al-taḥrīm): The act of making something forbidden; in marriage context, it can be a form of divorce.
لغو (laghw): Void; having no legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a husband says 'I am bain from you' (أنا منك بائن) with intention, what is the ruling?
A) It is void regardless of intention.
B) It is effective and she becomes bain.
C) It is effective only if he adds 'haram'.
D) It is considered a single revocable divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, divorce phrases must be directed at the wife; 'I am divorced from you' is void, while 'I am bain from you' and 'you are haram upon me' are valid with intention.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'You are Divorced Once or Not' and the Principle of Wording in Talaq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on uncertainty in talaq number

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the phrase 'أنت طالق واحدة أو لا', explain the principle of occurrence by number or adjective vs. by the word 'طالق', and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
When the number is uncertain, the divorce is void according to the Two, but a single revocable talaq occurs according to Muhammad.

The phrase 'أنت طالق واحدة أو لا' creates ambiguity about the number of divorces. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf consider the entire statement void because the occurrence is tied to the number, while Imam Muhammad argues it effects a single revocable divorce. This lesson explores the reasoning behind each position and the broader principle of how words impact talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed statement
The passage deals with statements like 'أنت طالق واحدة أو لا', 'مع موتي', etc. The matn rules them as void (لغو).
Similar phrases include 'أو لا شيء' and 'أو غير طالق'.
2
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Two) hold the statement is void, no talaq occurs. Muhammad holds it occurs as a single revocable talaq.
The mufta bihi is the view of the Two, as per the matn.
3
Examine the proofs for each view
The Two cite consensus on 'أنت طالق ثلاثاً' to show occurrence is by number; uncertainty in number voids. Muhammad uses examples like 'أنت طالق ومن واحدة إن شاء الله' and death before number to argue that occurrence is by 'طالق' and the number is merely a description.
The passage also mentions broader principles from al-Muhit and al-Khaniyah.
4
Understand the principle of wording
When the husband uses a specific adjective (e.g., 'البتة', 'للسنة') or a number, the occurrence of talaq is attributed to that adjective or number. If the adjective is omitted or conditions prevent it, the default is a single revocable talaq by the word 'طالق'.
This is shown by the dying wife or slave examples.
5
Apply to other cases
The same principle applies to 'أنت طالق ثلاثاً أولاً' (disputed) and 'أنت طالق أو لا' (void according to the Two). The passage also discusses 'خط الله' as an obscure phrase.
The thamarah al-khilaf: under the Two, no divorce; under Muhammad, one revocable divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (أنت طالق واحدة أو لا أو مع موتى أو مع موتك لغو) أما الأول فهو قولهما. وقال محمد: يقع رجعية لصرف الشك إلى الواحدة ولهما أن الوصف متى قرن بالعدد كان الوقوع بالعدد بدليل ما أجمع عليه من أنه لو قال لغير المدخول بها أنت طالق ثلاثاً طلقت ثلاثاً، ولو كان الوقوع بطالق لبانت لا إلى عدة فيلغو العدد. أنه لو قال أنت طالق ومن واحدة إن شاء الله لم يقع شيء، ولو كان الوقوع بطالق لكان العدد فاصلاً فوقع. ومن أنها لو ماتت قبل العدد لم يقع شيء كما سيأتي . ثم اعلم أن الوقوع أيضاً بالمصدر عند ذكره وكذا الوقوع بالصفة عند ذكرها كما إذا قال أنت طالق البتة كان الوقوع بالبتة حتى لو قال بعدها إن شاء الله متصلاً لا يقع، ولو كان الوقوع باسم الفاعل لوقع ويدل عليه ما في المحيط : لو قال أنت طالق للسنة أو أنت طالق بائن فماتت قبل أن يقول للسنة أو بائن لا يقع شيء لأنه صفة للإيقاع لا للتطليقة فيتوقف الإيقاع على ذكر الصفة، وأنه لا يتصور بعد الموت ا هـ . ويدل عليه بالأولى ما في الخانية من العتق رجل قال لعبده أنت حر البتة فمات العبد قبل أن يقول البتة فإنه يموت عبداً ا.هـ. ومراده من الواحدة مطلق العدد فلو قال أنت طالق ثلاثاً أولاً على الخلاف وقيدنا بالعدد لأنه لو قال أنت طالق أولاً لا يقع في قولهم. وفي المحيط : لو قال أنت طالق أو غير طالق أو أنت طالق أو لا شيء أو أنت طالق أو لا، لا قوله: (وروی خط (الله قال في النهر : الخط من الخطيطة وهي أرض لم تمطر . كذا في الدراية .
His statement: 'You are divorced once or not, or upon my death or upon your death, is void.' As for the first (case), it is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa). Muhammad said: It occurs as a revocable divorce, because the doubt is directed to the one (i.e., the divorce is considered to be once). The two hold that when the description is coupled with the number, the occurrence is by the number, as evidenced by the consensus that if he says to a woman not yet consummated 'you are divorced three', she becomes divorced thrice. If the occurrence were by the word 'divorced' (طالق), she would become irrevocably divorced without waiting period, and the number would be void. Also, if he says 'you are divorced and one in shaa Allah', nothing occurs; if it were by 'divorced', the number would be a disconnector and it would occur. And also that if she dies before the number, nothing would occur, as will come. Then know that the occurrence is also by the verbal noun (مصدر) when mentioned, and likewise by the adjective (صفة) when mentioned, as when he says 'you are divorced entirely (البتة)', the occurrence is by 'البتة'; even if he says afterwards 'in shaa Allah' continuously, it does not occur. If the occurrence were by the active participle (اسم فاعل), it would occur. Evidence for this is from al-Muhit: if he says 'you are divorced for the sunnah' or 'you are divorced bain', and she dies before he says 'for the sunnah' or 'bain', nothing occurs, because it is an adjective for the utterance of divorce, not for the talaqa itself, so the utterance is contingent upon mentioning the adjective, and that cannot be conceived after death. This is also supported by a case in al-Khaniyah regarding manumission: a man says to his slave 'you are free entirely' and the slave dies before he says 'entirely', then he dies as a slave. And his intent by 'one' (الواحدة) is absolute number; if he says 'you are divorced three' first (?) on the dispute, and we restrict it to number because if he says 'you are divorced first', it does not occur in their view. In al-Muhit: if he says 'you are divorced or not divorced' or 'you are divorced or nothing' or 'you are divorced or no', no (divorce occurs). His statement: (and it is narrated: 'خط الله' (the line of Allah)? Al-Nahr said: 'الخط' from 'الخطيطة' meaning land that has not been rained upon. This is from al-Dirayah.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling when a man says to his wife 'أنت طالق واحدة أو لا' (you are divorced once or not) or 'مع موتي' (upon my death) etc. The matn says these are void. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (قولهما) hold that such statements are void because the description (البتة, etc.) when coupled with number, the occurrence is determined by the number, and if the number is uncertain, the divorce does not take effect. Imam Muhammad, however, argues that it occurs as a revocable divorce, because the doubt (الشك) is resolved in favor of the number one (الواحدة) as the minimum. He cites several proofs: (1) consensus on 'you are divorced three' for a non-consummated wife; (2) if he says 'you are divorced and one in shaa Allah', nothing occurs; (3) if she dies before the number, nothing occurs. The passage then expands on the principle that the occurrence of divorce is by the specific wording ('بالمصدر' or 'بالصفة') rather than the root word 'طالق' alone, using examples of 'البتة' and 'للسنة' to show that the adjective qualifies the utterance and if omitted, the divorce is valid as a single revocable talaq? Actually the discussion concludes that when the adjective is mentioned, the occurrence is by that adjective, and if it is not mentioned, the divorce occurs by the word 'طالق' as a single revocable talaq. The passage also cites a parallel from manumission. Finally, it mentions that the word 'الواحدة' is interpreted as absolute number, and there is a dispute about 'ثلاثاً أولاً'.

Key Terms
البتة (al-battah): A term meaning 'entirely' or 'definitively', used to emphasize the divorce and make it irrevocable.
الرجعية (al-raj'iyyah): A revocable divorce where the husband can take back his wife during the waiting period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (قولهما), what is the ruling if a man says 'أنت طالق واحدة أو لا'?
A) It is a valid revocable divorce.
B) It is void; no divorce occurs.
C) It is an irrevocable divorce.
D) It is conditional upon the wife's acceptance.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, when uncertainty exists in the number of divorces, the default is that no talaq occurs unless the number is specified with certainty.

Ambiguous Divorce: 'One or No' – Void or Valid?
Explaining the ruling on ambiguous divorce with number and doubt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'You are divorced one or no' and explain the proof of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) versus Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
When number and doubt qualify 'taliq', occurrence is by the description, not the word — making the pronouncement void.

This lesson delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a divorce pronounced with ambiguity about the number. The matn rules it void, but Imam Muhammad considers it a valid raj'i divorce. Understanding their proofs sharpens your ability to analyze how description and intention interact in talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn ruling
The matn states that 'You are divorced one or no' is void (لغو). Recognize this as the starting point.
The commentary immediately introduces the dispute.
2
Attribute the views
The matn's ruling is attributed to 'the two' (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad holds it occurs as a raj'i divorce.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: the two vs. Muhammad.
3
Analyze the proof of the two
They argue that when a description (like number) is joined with 'taliq', occurrence is by the description. Evidence: consensus that saying 'You are divorced three' to an unconsummated wife makes it three, proving the number determines effect.
The proof uses consensus and qiyas to show the number is operative.
4
Analyze Muhammad's proof
Muhammad argues that the doubt is about the number only, so the basic divorce occurs as raj'i; the number is uncertain but the core word is effective.
He redirects the doubt to the description, not the essence.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is that of the two: the pronouncement is void. Muhammad's view is noted but not preferred.
Practical consequence: no divorce occurs; no iddah, no reconciliation needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحرام أنت طالق واحدة أو لا أو مع موتي أو مع موتك لغو ولو ملكها أو شقصها أنت مني بائن أو حرام أو أنا عليك حرام أو بائن ،وقع ولو قالت أنت بائن أو حرام ولم تقل مني فهو باطل. ووقع في بعض نسخ العيون: ولو قال بغير تاء التأنيث وظن صاحب الأكمل أنها مسألة مبتدأة وظن أنه لو قال ذلك الرجل لامرأته فهو باطل. وقال رضي الله تعالى عنه : وعند هذا ازداد سهواً شيخنا نجم الأئمة البخاري فزاد فيها لفظة «لها» فقال: لو قال لها أنت حرام أو بائن فهو باطل والمسألة. مع تاء التأنيث مذكورة في الواقعات الكبرى المدنية وغير المدنية في مسائل العيون فعرف به سهوهما ا.هـ. والحاصل من جهة الأحكام أنه إذا أضاف الحرمة أو البينونة إليها وقع من غير إضافة إليه وإن أضاف إلى نفسه لا يقع من غير إضافة إليها، وإن خيرها فأجابت بالحرمة أو البينونة فلا بد من الجمع بين الإضافتين أنت حرام علي، أنا حرام عليك أنت بائن مني أنا بائن منك والله سبحانه وتعالى الموفق . وقد حكى في المعراج في مسألة أنا منك طالق أن امرأة قالت لزوجها لو كان إلي ما إليك لرأيت الله ماذا أصنع فقال جعلت ما إلي إليك فقالت طلقتك فرفع ذلك إلى ابن عباس رضي عنهما فقال : خطأ الله نوءها هلا قالت طلقت نفسي منك، وروي خط الله وصوبه النسفي ،وقال : لا يجوز خطأ، وصاحب الفائق عكسه. والنوء كوكب تستمطر به العرب ا هـ . قوله : (أنت طالق واحدة أو لا أو مع موتي أو مع موتك لغو) أما الأول فهو قولهما. وقال محمد: يقع رجعية لصرف الشك إلى الواحدة ولهما أن الوصف متى قرن بالعدد كان الوقوع بالعدد بدليل ما أجمع عليه من أنه لو قال لغير المدخول بها أنت طالق ثلاثاً طلقت ثلاثاً، ولو كان الوقوع بطالق لبانت لا إلى عدة فيلغو العدد. أنه لو قال أنت طالق ومن واحدة إن شاء الله لم يقع شيء، ولو كان الوقوع بطالق لكان العدد فاصلاً فوقع. ومن أنها لو ماتت قبل العدد لم يقع شيء كما سيأتي .
And 'haram' and 'you are divorced one or no or with my death or with your death' are void. And if she said 'you are bain or haram' and did not say 'from me', it is invalid. And it occurs in some copies of Al-Uyun: 'and if he said without the feminine 'ta' and the author of Al-Akmal thought it was a new issue and thought that if a man said that to his wife it is invalid.' And he said, may Allah be pleased with him: 'And due to this, our Sheikh Najm al-A'imma al-Bukhari increased in forgetfulness by adding the word 'for her' and said: if he said to her 'you are haram or bain' it is invalid, while the issue with the feminine 'ta' is mentioned in Al-Waqi'at al-Kubra al-Madaniyya and others in the issues of Al-Uyun, so their forgetfulness is known by this.' And the summary from the perspective of rulings: if he attached the prohibition or separation to her, it occurs without attachment to himself; if he attached to himself, it does not occur without attachment to her; and if he gave her choice and she replied with prohibition or separation, it is necessary to combine both attachments: 'you are haram upon me, I am haram upon you, you are bain from me, I am bain from you.' And Allah Almighty is the Granter of success. And it is related in Al-Mi'raj regarding the issue 'I am divorced from you' that a woman said to her husband: 'If it were up to me like it is up to you, I would see what Allah would do.' He said: 'I have made what is up to me up to you.' She said: 'I divorced you.' This was raised to Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, and he said: 'May Allah put his star to the test (or 'make his speech err')—why didn't she say: I divorced myself from you?' And it is narrated 'Khatta Allah' and Al-Nasafi validated it and said: 'It is not permissible to say 'Khatta'' (as an error), while the author of Al-Faiq opposed him. And 'al-naw' is a star from which the Arabs seek rain. End. His saying: (You are divorced one or no or with my death or with your death is void) As for the first, it is the view of the two. And Muhammad said: It occurs as a raj'i divorce due to directing the doubt to the one; and for the two (the argument) is that when the description is joined with the number, the occurrence is by the number, as evidenced by consensus that if he said to a non-consummated wife 'you are divorced three', she is divorced thrice; if the occurrence were by 'taliq' she would become bain without waiting period, so the number becomes pointless. And also because if he said 'you are divorced and if one, God willing' nothing occurs; if the occurrence were by 'taliq', the number would be a separator and it would occur. And also because if she died before the number, nothing would occur, as will come.
Source pages p. 489

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a divorce pronouncement mixed with doubt. The matn states that if a man says 'You are divorced one or no' or similar phrases with doubt, the pronouncement is void (لغو). The commentary explains that this is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa? Actually it's قولهما, which in this context refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but then Muhammad is separately mentioned—so careful: the text says 'أما الأول فهو قولهما. وقال محمد: يقع رجعية' meaning that the ruling of void is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa? Standardly, قولهما refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, but here Muhammad is differing, so perhaps it's Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The commentary goes on to present Muhammad's argument that the divorce occurs as a raj'i (revocable) divorce because the doubt is considered to affect the number only, not the essence. The two argue that when a description (such as number) is attached to the word 'taliq', the occurrence is by the description itself, not by the word 'taliq'. They support this with consensus: if someone says to an unconsummated wife 'you are divorced three', she is divorced three times; if occurrence were by 'taliq', she would be irrevocably divorced without waiting period, making the number meaningless. They also cite that if he says 'you are divorced and if one, God willing', nothing occurs because the condition affects the number; and if she dies before the number, nothing occurs. Additionally, the passage includes an anecdote from Ibn Abbas about a woman who said 'I divorced you' instead of 'I divorced myself from you', and Ibn Abbas corrected her. The overall lesson is that in ambiguous divorce, the specific wording and intention matter greatly.

Key Terms
لغو (laghw): Void, having no legal effect; the divorce does not occur.
الوقوع (al-wuqu'): The occurrence of the divorce; whether the divorce takes effect.
رجعية (raj'iyyah): A revocable divorce; the husband can take back his wife during the waiting period without a new marriage.
الوصف (al-wasf): The description; the qualifying word (like number) attached to the divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn and the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa), what is the ruling if a man says to his wife 'أنت طالق واحدة أو لا' (You are divorced one or no)?
A) It is a valid raj'i divorce.
B) It is a valid bain divorce.
C) It is void (لغو) and no divorce occurs.
D) It is valid only if the wife accepts.

Key Takeaway
When a divorce pronouncement includes an ambiguous number, the Hanafi relied-upon ruling is that it is void, because the description (number) determines occurrence and its uncertainty nullifies the whole.
